           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/nye-2014-campaign-for-qt-gold-coast/">
             NYE 2014 campaign for QT Gold Coast
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           We all know QT Gold Coast as being  the venue for Queensland's "it" crowd. For their New Year's Eve campaign this year we drew on the TV series
           <em>
            Magic City
           </em>
           . Set in 1959 Miami, Florida shortly after the Cuban Revolution,
           <em>
            Magic City
           </em>
           tells the story of Ike Evans, the owner of Miamis most glamorous hotel, the Miramar Playa. Evans is forced to make an ill-fated deal with Miami mob boss Ben Diamond to ensure the success of his glitzy establishment.

            Read more

         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           NYE 2014 campaign for QT Gold Coast
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="537" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="537" data-imgheight-2="1075" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/109-201-Stingray-NYE-Blog_Graphic-540x537.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/109-201-Stingray-NYE-Blog_Graphic-1080x1075.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">

           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="702" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="702" data-imgheight-2="1404" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/109-201-Stingray-NYE-Blog_Poster-540x702.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/109-201-Stingray-NYE-Blog_Poster-1080x1404.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">

           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="341" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="341" data-imgheight-2="682" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/109-201-Stingray-NYE-Blog_Website-540x341.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/109-201-Stingray-NYE-Blog_Website-1080x682.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="NYE 2014 campaign for QT Gold Coast" height="536" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/109-201-Stingray-NYE-Blog_Website-850x536.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Paradise City  NYE 2014
          </h2>
          <p>
           We all know QT Gold Coast as being the venue for Queenslands it crowd. So for their New Years Eve campaign this year we drew inspiration from the TV series
           <em>
            Magic City
           </em>
           , known for its highly styled costumes and locations.
          </p>
          <p>
           Set in 1959 Miami, Florida shortly after the Cuban Revolution,
           <em>
            Magic City
           </em>
           tells the story of Ike Evans, the owner of Miamis most glamorous hotel, the Miramar Playa. It mixes both superficial luxury and a seedy underbelly with equal aplomb.
          </p>
          <p>
           The creative evoked the nostalgic Miami scene with its cool pastel colour scheme and iconic art deco type style. All in all, an exotic, electric and sexy campaign for the biggest night on the QT calendar.
          </p>
          <p>
           If youd like to attend find out more about the event on the QT Gold Coast
           <a href="http://www.qtgoldcoast.com.au/qt-life/party-like-1959-new-years-eve-qt-gold-coast/" target="_blank">
            website
           </a>
           .
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          3 December 2014
         </time>

           <noscript>
            <img alt="Zoofari 2014 Event Branding" height="512" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/109-186-Taronga-Event-Blog_Tiger-Zoofari-850x512.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Our journey of creative partnership with Taronga Zoo
          </h2>
          <p>
           Another Colour have supported fundraising events by Taronga Zoo, delivering imaginative new design solutions for many events over the last five years.
          </p>
          <p>
           We have grown close to each cause and feel rewarded as funds are raised, aiding in the conservation of a wide range of animals, both local and abroad.
          </p>
          <p>
           The design features that made the event branding for each occasion memorable, motivating and moving have been mapped out below on a timeline.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Zoofari 2010  Year of the Tiger
          </h2>
          <p>
           Upon removing a golden belly band, the reader came face-to-face with a Tiger. Once unfurled, the invitee held in their hands the last 400 Sumatran Tigers left in the wild, each tigers silhouette hand-drawn and gold foiled.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/projects/year-of-the-tiger/">
            See more images of this project here.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           Taronga Dinner 2011  Wild Frontiers
          </h2>
          <p>
           A series of exotic landscapes appeared throughout the invitation, with a stark, white silhouette reversed from the photographs representing a missing animal. It invited the audience to imagine a world in which animals did not exist.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Zoofari 2011  Black and White Lemur Ball
          </h2>
          <p>
           The playful nature of these animals was captured as the invitation was unrolled to reveal the Lemurs story on one side and a full-scale replica of the distinctive Lemur tail on the other.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/projects/lemur-black-white-ball/">
            See more images of this project here.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           Taronga Dinner 2012  Leap for Survival
          </h2>
          <p>
           With fewer than 120 Corroboree Frogs left in the wild, a strong message was required with this event invitation. A carefully die cut pocket referencing frog eggs is removed to reveal a small number of baby frogs within.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/projects/leap-for-survival/">
            See more images of this project here.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           Zoofari 2012  Five for the Wild
          </h2>
          <p>
           A cascade of flowing watercolour and pen illustration graced this invitation to create a visual feast, celebrating the Asian Elephant, Cassowary, African Wild Dog, Sumatran Tiger and the Platypus. The result was a set of colourful pieces with differing textural elements, set to bold and classic typefaces.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/projects/five-for-the-wild/">
            See more images of this project here.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           Zoofari 2013  Cherishing Chimps
          </h2>
          <p>
           This invitation used the nostalgia of collage, incorporating Tarongas Chimps and vintage drawings of exotic flora to raise awareness for the destruction of habitat facing the Chimpanzee in equatorial Africa.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/projects/cherish-our-chimps/">
            See more images of this project here.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           Taronga Dinner 2014  Elephant Journey
          </h2>
          <p>
           We used a unique gate fold and ornate asian imagery for Elephant Journey to suggest a new door opening for young-adult Elephants as they make a new home at Western Plains Zoo. As you opened the cover, it revealed two elephants embracing on the inside spread. Regal golds and cool aqua colours featured heavily, paired with a classic typeface.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Zoofari 2014  Tiger Zoofari
          </h2>
          <p>
           This year saw us come full circle with tigers. The concept drew upon art history from cultures all over the globe and captured tigers in diverse artworks, from varying periods to celebrate their diversity and history.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Our creative legacy. Their charitable successes.
          </h2>
          <p>
           This inspired partnership would not have been possible without the assistance of Jess and her predecessor Rebecca, Burwood Press and all the Taronga team for allowing us to create, develop and be such a big part of bringing these important events to life. Thanks to their efforts and our design solutions future generations will live to see these animals continue to exist.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          2 December 2014
         </time>

           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="394" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="394" data-imgheight-2="788" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_f-540x394.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_f-1080x788.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Design Tools" height="620" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_f-850x620.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="394" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="394" data-imgheight-2="788" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_g-540x394.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_g-1080x788.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Font Game" height="620" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_g-850x620.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="711" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="711" data-imgheight-2="1422" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_h-540x711.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_h-1080x1422.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Visualator" height="1119" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_h-850x1119.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="685" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="685" data-imgheight-2="1370" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_i-540x685.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_i-1080x1370.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Behance" height="1078" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_i-850x1078.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="960" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="960" data-imgheight-2="1920" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_j-540x960.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_j-1080x1920.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Snapseed" height="1511" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_j-850x1511.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="405" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="405" data-imgheight-2="810" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_k-540x405.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_k-1080x810.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Shape CC" height="637" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_k-850x637.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="539" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="539" data-imgheight-2="1079" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_l-540x539.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_l-1080x1079.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Catwang" height="849" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-182-Designer-Apps-Blog-Post_l-850x849.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <p>
           Another Colour handpicks our 12 must-have apps to keep every graphic designer inspired and entertained.
          </p>
          <h2>
           1. Oko
          </h2>
          <p>
           Stunning satellite images are turned into psychedelic puzzles. This free app contains 20 unique images that are segmented into circles and spin at varying speeds. Not recommended if youre nursing a hangover! Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/oko/id524351381?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS
           </a>
           or
           <a href="https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=cc.openframeworks.OKO" target="_blank">
            Android.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           2. Monument Valley
          </h2>
          <p>
           Were a big fan of impossible shapes so we loved the graphic illusions on offer in this beautifully illustrated adventure game. Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/monument-valley/id728293409?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS
           </a>
           or
           <a href="https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.ustwo.monumentvalley" target="_blank">
            Android.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           3. Trend Generator
          </h2>
          <p>
           Trend Generator allows you to create posters on the fly, using design trends that have been catalogued on trendlist.org. Type on a path, gradient, diagonal pattern are just some examples of the hipster treatments you can apply to your designs. Its definitely more style over substance, but its still a bit of fun. Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/trend-generator/id767377188?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           4. Logos Quiz
          </h2>
          <p>
           Fancy yourself as a bit of a logo nerd? This app is loaded with over 900 famous (and some obscure) brands that have been partially hidden. Can you guess them all?
           <br/>
           Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/logos-quiz-game/id478364212?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           5. Adobe Color CC
          </h2>
          <p>
           Stuck for a colour? Adobe Color CC ( formerly Kuler) is our go-to app for generating harmonious palettes. One of its key features is the ability to add swatches from a photograph, and easily sync them with the Adobe suite. We especially love the way you can share your favourite palettes with the rest of the design community.
           <br/>
           Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/adobe-color-cc-capture-color/id632313714?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           6. Design Tools
          </h2>
          <p>
           Consider this the bible for every graphic designer. This handy app houses lots of useful information such as standard page sizes, unit conversion, and even a golden ratio calculator.
           <br/>
           Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/design-tools/id524121736?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           7. The Font Game
          </h2>
          <p>
           Know your Gothams from your Garamonds? Put your typeface knowledge to the test with this satisfyingly geeky game. If youre a pro, you can take it to the next level and complete the font terminology quiz. Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/the-font-game/id344065205?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           8. Visualator
          </h2>
          <p>
           Create mind-bending abstract graphics with this fun tool developed by the guys at Computer Arts magazine. Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/computer-arts-visualator/id401118791?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           9. Behance
          </h2>
          <p>
           Behance is one of the studios favourite resources for inspirationand it turns out they have a pretty neat iPhone app too. Great for that train ride in to work when youre looking for that creative spark to get you going. Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/behance/id489667151?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS
           </a>
           or
           <a href="https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.behance.behance&amp;hl=en" target="_blank">
            Android.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           10. Snapseed
          </h2>
          <p>
           Transform your smart phone snaps into re-touched pieces of art with this handy app were labelling Instagram on steroids. Whether its subtle colour correction or a dramatic filter, Snapseed can do it all  Youll never need another photo editor again. Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/snapseed/id439438619?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS
           </a>
           or
           <a href="https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.niksoftware.snapseed&amp;hl=en">
            Android.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           11. Shape CC
          </h2>
          <p>
           Embrace your inner-Warhol and create vectorised high contrast images using just your smart phone. You can then easily sync with Creative Coud and incorporate into your designs.
           <br/>
           Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/adobe-shape-cc-capture-create/id919014644?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           12. Catwang
          </h2>
          <p>
           Create meme-worthy collages using Catwangs library of laser beams, pizza slices and you guessed it..cats. Scale, rotate and flip the various elements and create your own bizarre scenes before sharing them with your instagram and facebook followers. Download for
           <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/catwang-super-awesome-sticker/id511664488?mt=8" target="_blank">
            iOS.
           </a>
          </p>
          <h2>
           Think weve missed some?
          </h2>
          <p>
           Wed love to hear from you, let us know via the Another Colour
           <a href="https://www.facebook.com/anothercolourstudio" target="_blank">
            facebook page.
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          27 November 2014
         </time>

           12 of Historys Greatest Graphic Designers
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="414" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="414" data-imgheight-2="828" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-167-Historys-Greatest-Graphic-Designers1-540x414.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-167-Historys-Greatest-Graphic-Designers1-1080x828.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">

          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="394" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="394" data-imgheight-2="789" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-167-Historys-Greatest-Graphic-Designers2-540x394.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-167-Historys-Greatest-Graphic-Designers2-1080x789.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">

          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="338" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="338" data-imgheight-2="676" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-167-Historys-Greatest-Graphic-Designers3-540x338.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-167-Historys-Greatest-Graphic-Designers3-1080x676.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="12 of Historys Greatest Graphic Designers" height="532" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-167-Historys-Greatest-Graphic-Designers3-850x532.jpg" width="850"/>

          </figure>

           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="354" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="354" data-imgheight-2="709" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-167-Historys-Greatest-Graphic-Designers6-540x354.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-167-Historys-Greatest-Graphic-Designers6-1080x709.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="12 of Historys Greatest Graphic Designers" height="558" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/109-167-Historys-Greatest-Graphic-Designers6-850x558.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           We stand on the shoulders of giants
          </h2>
          <p>
           Within graphic design, our kind are not as widely celebrated as high achieving individuals from other creative industries, despite our contribution to the visual environment. There are no widely publicised awards shows with red carpets and little statues, or major articles devoted to the work we do, with our names and faces splashed across the pages.
          </p>
          <p>
           However, most of you will be familiar with the creative output of some of those with a higher profile  the pioneers in our field. And today we want to focus on the stars that shone bright, often far from the spotlight, the ones whose work needs to be discussed, pawed-over and mined for inspiration.
          </p>
          <p>
           Although our industry is relatively young, there is a rich pool of talented lumineers from recent history that we can all draw upon for daily creative cues. Let us introduce you to twelve designers who have a far greater influence over current graphic styles than many people realise.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Paul Rand (1914  1996)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Even after his passing, Paul Rand endures as one of the most influential graphic designers in the world. To a certain degree, his renowned corporate identity designs for companies like IBM, ABC, UPS and Westinghouse are the reason for such status within the design community.
          </p>
          <p>
           Rand began his career designing covers for
           <em>
            Direction
           </em>
           magazine, where he embraced and honed the Swiss Style of graphic design, a practice developed in 1950s Switzerland and known for its emphases on clean lines, readability and objectivity. He was inducted into the New York Art Directors Club Hall of Fame in 1972.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Saul Bass (Born 1920  1996)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Mr Bass was primarily a graphic designer but is best known for his work on animated motion picture title sequences, for
           <em>
            Psycho, Anatomy of a Murder, Spartacus
           </em>
           and
           <em>
            The Man with the Golden Arm
           </em>
           . These are the best examples of his film work and of the style at large.
          </p>
          <p>
           He was responsible for memorable logos like the AT&amp;T globe, Minolta, United Airlines, The Girl Scouts and later he would also produce logos for numerous Japanese companies. In addition to this enviable portfolio, Bass designed the pared back poster for the 1984 Los Angeles Olympic Games and several Academy Awards shows.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Milton Glaser (Born 1929)
          </h2>
          <p>
           The name may not be familiar to most but the many iconic works he created are still being worn to this day  his ubiquitous I Heart NY shirt), or well-thumbed through (New York Magazine). Then there is the psychedelic Bob Dylan poster and the DC comics logo. Mr Glasers work is consistently characterised by simplicity and originality.
          </p>
          <p>
           Not only did Milton Glaser create a visual feast for successive generations of designers, he also spoke succinct, wise words that all creatives can use as a modern day mantra  The real issue is not talent as an independent element, but talent in relationship to will, desire, and persistence. Talent without these things vanishes and even modest talent with those characteristics grows.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Massimo Vignelli (1931  2014)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Massimo Vignelli tells us that if you can design one thing, you can design everything. And his lifes work is a testament to these inspiring words. His portfolio includes packaging design, furniture design, interior design, architectural and exhibition graphics, product design and last but not least, graphic design.
          </p>
          <p>
           Vignellis most familiar work however was his design for the NYC Subway system and the DC Metro system signage. He also imparts his wisdom teaching and lecturing on design in the major cities and universities in the United States and abroad.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Deborah Sussman (1931  2014)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Deborah Sussman was best known for leading the team that created the environmental graphics of the 1984 Summer Olympics in Los Angeles. The team created bold, brightly colored supergraphics  large scale designs that were shaped around the built environment and gave the urban landscape a vibrancy and the architecture a much needed makeover. This characteristic technique that she pioneered and more is more mantra has since gone mainstream, allowing other designers to realise information signage in non-traditional ways.
          </p>
          <p>
           Her bold graphics reflected her unspoken dialogue with clients, best articulated here: Several people have told me over the years just give them what they want with regards to clients, and I cant bring myself to do it, I have to inspire them, and that can sometimes be a very dangerous attitude to have because you can lose yourself a lot of money.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Ruth Ansel (Born 1938)
          </h2>
          <p>
           As the visionary art director of prestigious titles such as
           <em>
            Harpers Bazaar
           </em>
           in the 1960s,
           <em>
            The New York Times Magazine
           </em>
           in the 1970s,
           <em>
            Vanity Fair
           </em>
           and
           <em>
            Vogue
           </em>
           in the 1980s; she has collaborated with nearly every icon of magazine publishing including Diana Vreeland, Annie Leibowitz, Bruce Weber and a whole lot more. But all of this was only part of her creative output during an illustrious career. She also directed fashion ad campaigns for Versace, Club Monaco and Karl Lagerfield.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Paula Scher (Born 1948)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Femme fatale Scher began her graphic design career as an art director for record covers at both Atlantic and CBS Records and became known as an innovative typographer, shunning the ever present Helvetica.
          </p>
          <p>
           This wild side is balanced with her corporate identity work for iconic brands like Tiffany &amp; Co., Citibank, New York City Ballet; Bloomberg, Coca-Cola, the Metropolitan Opera, and MoMA. She is now continuing her legacy, shaping young minds as an educator at the School of Visual Arts (SVA) in New York.
          </p>
          <h2>
           David Carson (Born 1954)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Rough, rugged and raw, Carson, once considered an upstart in the design world, rose to prominence in the grunge era. Known for his anti-swiss style, through an abstract cut and paste aesthetic that could even be described as noisey. A style he started in Transworld Skateboarding and perfected with Ray Gun magazine.
          </p>
          <p>
           His experiments with design have led him to break widely observed graphic design rules in regards to grids, typography and its interplay with imagery. This playful technique of freeform creation in various mediums has ensured a vitality and a longevity for his career.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Neville Brody (Born 1957)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Neville Brodys meteoric rise began with his incredible art direction of cult UK magazine
           <em>
            The Face
           </em>
           between 1981 and 1986, establishing it as a doyen of culture and style. And as the creative force behind
           <em>
            Arena
           </em>
           magazine his stature within the publishing world was cemented.
          </p>
          <p>
           This master typographer used type as a primary element of the hero image, even creating the image itself entirely from letterforms. Although the magazine was his bread and butter work he often stepped away from the printed page to design record covers for artists such as Cabaret Voltaire and Depeche Mode to name but a few.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Stefan Sagmeister (Born 1962)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Enfant terrible, only in the best kind of way, Stefan Sagmeister pushes the boundaries like no other designer. Most notably is the 1999 poster for AIGA where he had his assistant carve the letters into his torso with a knife, photographing the bloody mess for all to see.
          </p>
          <p>
           Born in Austria, he now lives in New York City where he dabbles in the music scene, designing album covers for Lou Reed, OK Go, The Rolling Stones, David Byrne and Aerosmith.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Chip Kidd ( Born 1964)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Primarily a book jacket designer Chip Kidd has freelanced for many of the major publishing houses such as Penguin, Amazon and Random House; working with noted authors like Bret Easton Ellis, Haruki Murakami, Cormac McCarthy, Frank Miller and David Sedaris. He has often devalued the importance of his designs, expressing of his role, Im very much against the idea that the cover will sell the book. We disagree, and feel it is the perfect introduction to an undiscovered author.
          </p>
          <p>
           Because, you can tell a book by its cover, at least when Kidd is at the helm. He has a way of arresting the readers gaze, with art that speaks volumes for the printed word inside with one single image. His striking style has sometimes transcended the literary world, to be featured on marketing material for the film adaptation of Michael Crichtons
           <em>
            Jurassic Park
           </em>
           novel.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Deanne Cheuk (Born 1975)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Although our very own Deanne Cheuk now resides in New York she is native to Perth, Western Australia. She has many design arrows in her quiver  illustrator, designer, art director and artist. But the world of publishing is where she is most at home as contributor to Nippon Vogue, Dazed &amp; Confused, Nylon, Black Book, The Fader, Flaunt, Tokion and The New York Times Magazine.
          </p>
          <p>
           Cheuk pioneered the use of illustrative typography with her oft-copied/rarely-bettered style of watercolour titles and hand drawn letterforms on the printed page. This has led to commissioned work for revered companies like Nike, Converse, Swatch, The Gap, MTV, Levis, Nickelodeon, Nokia, and Converse.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Their Visual Legacy
          </h2>
          <p>
           As pillars of the design community, the impact is still apparent to this day. Their classic creations can help you navigate your train journey, be worn on an iconic tourist t-shirt, they package up your products and make your Sunday reading more pleasing to the eye.
          </p>
          <p>
           Moreover it is a testament to their skills that many current-day creatives still look to these masters for inspiration. Serving as models for modern-day designs, evolving from templates set out decades earlier.
          </p>
          <p>
           Often unchanged since genesis, the works of these designers are immune to the shifting tide of trends. Each name a permanent synonym for style.
          </p>
          <p>
           <em>
            Sources
           </em>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://adcglobal.org/awards/hall-of-fame" target="_blank">
            adcglobal.org/awards/hall-of-fame
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://aiga.org/medalist-saulbass" target="_blank">
            aiga.org/medalist-saulbass
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://quotesondesign.com/milton-glaser-7" target="_blank">
            quotesondesign.com/milton-glaser-7
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://abduzeedo.com/5-lessons-massimo-vignelli" target="_blank">
            abduzeedo.com/5-lessons-massimo-vignelli
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://fastcodesign.com/3034682" target="_blank">
            fastcodesign.com/3034682
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://ruthansel.com" target="_blank">
            ruthansel.com
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://aiga.org/medalist-paulascher" target="_blank">
            aiga.org/medalist-paulascher
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://davidcarsondesign.com" target="_blank">
            davidcarsondesign.com
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://designishistory.com/1980/neville-brody" target="_blank">
            designishistory.com/1980/neville-brody
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://sagmeisterwalsh.com" target="_blank">
            sagmeisterwalsh.com
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://wikipedia.org/wiki/Chip_Kidd" target="_blank">
            wikipedia.org/wiki/Chip_Kidd
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://deannecheuk.com" target="_blank">

           </a>
          </p>
         </div>

        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Win a double pass to Taronga Zoo. 10 to be won!
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="540" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="540" data-imgheight-2="960" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/109-181-Zoo-Comp-Artwork_3-540x540.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/109-181-Zoo-Comp-Artwork_3.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="960">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Win tickets to Taronga Zoo" height="850" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/109-181-Zoo-Comp-Artwork_3-850x850.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Simply answer the following question
          </h2>
          <p>
           If you could choose any animal in the entire world to be your pet, what would it be and what name would you give it?
           <br/>
           The most interesting, humorous or creative answers win.
          </p>
          <p>
           For example Greg the Lemur or Marilyn the Marmoset.
          </p>
          <p>
           Winners announced 27 October 2014. Entries to be received by comments on the
           <a href="http://www.facebook.com/anothercolourstudio" target="_blank">
            Another Colour Facebook page
           </a>
           only. Terms and conditions apply and can be
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/taronga-comp" target="_blank">
            found here
           </a>
           .
          </p>
         </div>

          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/10-vintage-vogue-covers-that-make-todays-look-dull/">
             10 Vintage Vogue cover designs that make todays look dull
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           Before the power of celebrity endorsement and the importance of brand recognition, what did the cover of Vogue once look like? Another Colour took a peek back in time at the British Vogue Archive to reveal how the cover of one of the most revered magazines in the world has evolved over time.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/10-vintage-vogue-covers-that-make-todays-look-dull/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">
           5 September 2014
          </time>
          <aside>
           <ul>
            <li class="inspiration">
             <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/filter/inspiration/">
             </a>
            </li>
           </ul>
          </aside>

       </div>

         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           10 Vintage Vogue cover designs that make todays look dull
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">

           <noscript>

          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="711" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="711" data-imgheight-2="1422" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Another-Colour-Vintage-Vogue-Handdrawn-5-540x711.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Another-Colour-Vintage-Vogue-Handdrawn-5-1080x1422.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Vogue Cover February 1935" height="1119" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Another-Colour-Vintage-Vogue-Handdrawn-5-850x1119.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="355" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="355" data-imgheight-2="711" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Another-Colour-Vintage-Vogue-21st-6-540x355.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Another-Colour-Vintage-Vogue-21st-6-1080x711.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Vogue Covers September 1937 and June 1944" height="559" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Another-Colour-Vintage-Vogue-21st-6-850x559.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="711" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="711" data-imgheight-2="1422" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Another-Colour-Vintage-Vogue-Dali-7-540x711.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Another-Colour-Vintage-Vogue-Dali-7-1080x1422.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Vogue Cover June 1944" height="1119" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Another-Colour-Vintage-Vogue-Dali-7-850x1119.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Vogue BC (Before Celebrity)
          </h2>
          <p>
           Earlier this year, Anna Wintour placed a reality television star and her husband on the cover of American Vogue. The use of celebrities on Vogue (and magazine covers in general) has become a powerful selling tool; familiar faces and oversized taglines scream at readers to buy me.
          </p>
          <p>
           But before the power of celebrity endorsement and the importance of brand recognition, what did the cover of Vogue once look like? Another Colour took a peek back in time at the
           <a href="http://www.vogue.co.uk/magazine/archive" target="_blank">
            British Vogue Archive
           </a>
           to reveal how the cover of one of the most revered magazines in the world has evolved over time.
          </p>
          <h2>
           June 1917
          </h2>
          <p>
           She may have been very curvy or she may have been drowning in trim, but undoubtedly the June 1917 cover by George Wolfe Plank offered readers unabashed escapism from World War 1. Almost in spite of the war and a possible testament to the need for people to find some form of solace or distraction from general social bleakness, sales of the magazine were up during this period.
          </p>
          <h2>
           January 1923
          </h2>
          <p>
           This really was the dawn of the golden age of fashion illustration: each cover was a work of art that explored colour, shape and drew the eye in with rich details. Here a model appears to be feeding a dragon marshmallows.
          </p>
          <p>
           Only the masthead has any resemblance to the current version of Vogue, in a similar font (Baskerville Old Face) that currently sits purposefully at the top of each issue. But that hasnt always been a fixed feature
          </p>
          <h2>
           September 1926
          </h2>
          <p>
           The Roaring 20s brought with it a whole new variety of cover art  literally, art, including this lavish September 1926 cover by Art Deco artist, Benito. Covers started to explore more detailed forms of expression, including the use of intricate backgrounds, landscapes and even architecture.
          </p>
          <h2>
           July 1928
          </h2>
          <p>
           By the late 20s, every issue featured the masthead reborn in an entirely new form, using many different fonts. And some without an actual font at all, instead incorporating features of the cover art such as extra long scarf knots in the wind or parting clouds clouds that would reveal the word, Vogue.
          </p>
          <h2>
           October 1930
          </h2>
          <p>
           Following the exuberance of the 20s, the 30s brought with it The Great Depression. This, however, didnt prevent Vogue from maintaining their sense of celebration and art during these tough times. Here, the cover of October 1930 sits somewhere between Art Deco and Surrealism in simple and pared back hues of austere beige.
          </p>
          <h2>
           July 1932
          </h2>
          <p>
           It was their 1932 July issue that featured their first ever photographic cover. It was shot by Edward Steichen, although he was not credited for his work at the time, and it featured a woman in a bright red swimsuit sitting against a background of cobalt blue. What is most remarkable, we feel, about this image is that the photographic medium was still used to portray artistic movements that were happening at the time: the ongoing influence of cubism is apparent in the harsh shadows that appear on the swimsuit model and her face, which emphasises the length and positioning of the body that resembles geometric shapes. It would still be some years yet before the photograph became the accepted norm for Vogues covers.
          </p>
          <h2>
           February 1935
          </h2>
          <p>
           For the February edition, 1935, Carl Erickson  a fashion illustrator for over 35 years  offered a stark watercolour cover that looks little more than a doodle, with the masthead scribbled across the top. We cant really see Anna Wintour approving something like this.
          </p>
          <h2>
           September 1937
          </h2>
          <p>
           For the UK editions 21st anniversary issue a birthday cake and unicorn were designed. They appear to be floating romantically in the sky, painted in purple and powder blue  a cover as far removed from fashion ever seen on Vogue. Although it does have a rather Vivienne Westwood feel to it.
          </p>
          <h2>
           August 1940
          </h2>
          <p>
           On the August 1940 cover, model  Lisa Fonssagrives was photographed wearing a boy-cut swimsuit and used her own body to pose as letters, spelling out the Vogue magazine title. The cover was recreated in 1992 for British Vogues 75th Anniversary issue.
          </p>
          <h2>
           June 1944
          </h2>
          <p>
           Dals surrealist cover of April 1944 arrives during the throes of World War 2. It is one of the final few covers to escape the soon to be standardised format: fixed serif masthead; photograph of a female model, usually maintaining eye contact with her audience; and some catchy captions intended to attract a greater readership. By the 1950s, the cover achieved the formulaic template we are now so familiar with.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Vogue Today
          </h2>
          <p>
           We understand that Vogue is a business, and each editor has redirected the magazine to ensure its longevity and a highly successful brand but, looking back, we cant help but feel that a particular magic and appeal was lost along with the more creative artwork that once graced Vogues cover. Its sad that each issues cover is no longer a true blank canvas; a place where an illustrator or artist could take the reader far, far away from the burdens of a world driven by making a buck.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          5 September 2014
         </time>

            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-homage-to-shigeo-fukuda post-hidden-onload post-1170" data-postid="1170" data-title="Homage to Shigeo Fukuda :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Homage to Shigeo Fukuda
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="539" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="539" data-imgheight-2="1078" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/Another-Colour-Fakuda-Illustration_Arms-540x539.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/Another-Colour-Fakuda-Illustration_Arms-1080x1078.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Fakuda inspired illustration by Another Colour - hands" height="848" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/Another-Colour-Fakuda-Illustration_Arms-850x848.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="540" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="540" data-imgheight-2="1080" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/Fakuda-homage-illustration-scotch-soda-540x540.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/Fakuda-homage-illustration-scotch-soda-1080x1080.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Fakuda inspired illustration by Another Colour - scotch and soda" height="850" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/Fakuda-homage-illustration-scotch-soda-850x850.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="539" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="539" data-imgheight-2="1078" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/Another-Colour-Fakuda-Illustration_Hands-540x539.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/Another-Colour-Fakuda-Illustration_Hands-1080x1078.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Fakuda inspired illustration by Another Colour - fingers" height="848" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/Another-Colour-Fakuda-Illustration_Hands-850x848.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Reflections from the past can inform the present
          </h2>
          <p>
           Powerful design is a balance of arresting imagery and succinct messaging. And no one understands this better than Fukuda. Behind his bold, bright colouring is a distillation of complex ideas, often achieved through juxtaposition. Mens legs intertwine with womens, a new branch springs forth from an axe handle or corporate attire walks alongside psychedelic styling.
          </p>
          <p>
           With this in mind we proposed to create our own set of modest graphics, which are almost logo-like in their simplicity. Hopefully capturing some of that Fukuda genius in the process. We extended a cheeky middle finger on one, reflected with the two fingered peace sign. Scotch bottles sit alongside soda topped with straws. All with a distinctly 21st century colour palette.
          </p>
          <p>
           Fukuda also taught us other valuable lessons in design practice. His love of minimalism, asymmetry and sans serif typefaces served him well and, although he forged a signature style, he ensured that his unique aesthetic retained a classic timelessness decades later.
          </p>
          <p>
           As good designers we must remain vigilant, educating ourselves in the styles and substance of intelligent work that has come before, seeking out famed creatives who can inform us and our work in the modern age. Beautiful graphics are always more compelling with meaning.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          22 July 2014
         </time>

           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/a-room-with-a-view/">
             Environmental graphics for a Samsung product launch
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p dir='""""""""ltr""""""""'>
           Here at Another Colour we are often presented with a project to challenge the standard ways in which we are accustomed to designing. The work we completed for Event Emporium was no exception and rather than working with a single dimension such as graphics for print or screen we were required to think and design in three dimensions.
          </p>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-a-room-with-a-view post-hidden-onload post-1005" data-postid="1005" data-title="Environmental graphics for a Samsung product launch :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Environmental graphics for a Samsung product launch
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="359" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="359" data-imgheight-2="719" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-event-graphics-540x359.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-event-graphics-1080x719.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Exhibition Graphics for Samsung product launch" height="565" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-event-graphics-850x565.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="359" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="359" data-imgheight-2="719" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-wall-graphics-540x359.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-wall-graphics-1080x719.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Exhibition Graphics for the kitchen at a product launch" height="565" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-wall-graphics-850x565.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="359" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="359" data-imgheight-2="719" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-vinyl-graphics-540x359.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-vinyl-graphics-1080x719.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Exhibition Graphics for Samsung's speaker product launch" height="565" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-vinyl-graphics-850x565.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="359" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="359" data-imgheight-2="719" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-room-graphics-540x359.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-room-graphics-1080x719.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Exhibition Graphics for the living room at a product launch" height="565" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Samsung-room-graphics-850x565.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           A room with a view  designing a liveable space
          </h2>
          <p>
           Here at Another Colour we are often presented with a project to challenge the standard ways in which we are accustomed to designing. The work we completed for Event Emporium was no exception and rather than working with a single dimension such as graphics for print or screen we were required to think and design in three dimensions.
          </p>
          <p>
           Event Emporium commissioned us to flex our creative muscle for Samsung on a new product launch of the Audio Multiroom, an innovative new way to integrate wireless speakers so you, the listener, can enjoy music in many rooms at once. Such smart technology required a smart approach.
          </p>
          <p>
           We transformed an exhibition space, which featured a life-size replica of a home interior, whose stark white walls were graced with light grey vinyl decals of familiar household objects; and furnished with a white couch, bar and stools. All this was designed to draw the eye to the starring attraction, the exquisite black unit.
          </p>
          <p>
           The result was a resounding success. As any immersive experience, it took the audience through the space where they were able to see hear and feel the equipment first hand. The whole display spoke volumes about our ability as designers to adapt our design skills to the built environment.
          </p>
          <p>
           Event imagery courtesy of Event Emporium.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          24 June 2014
         </time>

       <div class="box article-wrapper thumb-slug-from-farm-to-fashion thumb-962 filter-news filter-project filter-all" data-postid="962">
        <div class="outer-listing">
         <div class="listing">
          <a class="blog-thumb" href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/from-farm-to-fashion/">
           <figure class="auto-size fade-image bg-color" data-autoheight="140" data-autowidth="250" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="140" data-imgheight-2="281" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-105-Mohair-Blog-Post1-250x140.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-105-Mohair-Blog-Post1-500x281.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="250" data-imgwidth-2="500">
            <noscript>
             <img alt="" height="140" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-105-Mohair-Blog-Post1-250x140.jpg" width="250"/>
            </noscript>
           </figure>
          </a>
          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/from-farm-to-fashion/">
             Exhibition signage at the Easter Show
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           This year Easter came early for us when we were requested to work with the Royal Agricultural Society of NSW on signage for The Royal Easter Show. Large scale images of wool, alpaca, cotton and angora graced the large-format graphics for The Natural Fibres Showcase along with products that are produced from these raw materials and a mix of modern and classic typefaces.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/from-farm-to-fashion/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">

           <noscript>
            <img alt="Another Colour's tour of the Royal Easter Show" height="286" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-105-Mohair-Blog-Post8-850x286.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           From farm to fashion
          </h2>
          <p>
           This year Easter came early for us when we were requested to work with the Royal Agricultural Society of NSW on signage for The Royal Easter Show. Large scale images of wool, alpaca, cotton and angora graced the large-format graphics for The Natural Fibres Showcase along with products that are produced from these raw materials and a mix of modern and classic typefaces.
          </p>
          <p>
           Two major components came together for the project: promotional banners and an interactive stand designed as an educational experience about Mohair.
          </p>
          <p>
           The promotional banners that teased people back to the Natural Fibre Showcase featured lifestyle photography and muted, earthy tones, with the key messages splashed across them  100% Natural, 100% Responsible and 100% Australian.
          </p>
          <p>
           At the Mohair stand the raw wool was interspersed with finished products such as jumpers and socks, photos from the farm and informational charts. All of this was designed to engage the customer in discussion around the process and benefits of using the natural over the artificial. This is essentially the key message of the show itself, use of Australian, all-natural products that are farmed and produced locally.
          </p>
          <p>
           We had the pleasure of being taken on a behind-the-scenes tour by our client Mike Burgess, to meet farm animals and speak directly to farmers, and last but not least, indulge our love of carnival rides and fairground food.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          22 May 2014
         </time>

          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-077-MFAA-Blog-Post_5-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-077-MFAA-Blog-Post_5-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Program design and event branding for MFAA" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-077-MFAA-Blog-Post_5-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <p>
           Designing for excellence
          </p>
          <p>
           At Another Colour we love a good challenge and this particular one was no exception to the rule. We designed an event identity and supporting collateral for
           <a href="http://www.eventemporium.com.au/" target="_blank">
            Event Emporium
           </a>
           , event managers of MFAAs gala dinner. As this was celebrating those in the industry who excel, the program had to be well in a word, excellent.
          </p>
          <p>
           The Commonwealth Bank was the major sponsor, so we drew inspiration from the brands colour palette and created a geometric pattern: a contemporary, yet timeless arrangement that tumbles across the cover and throughout the inner pages.
          </p>
          <p>
           From all reports the night was a big success, which can be seen in the photos above, supplied by Event Emporium. Its great to work alongside fellow creatives and watch it all come together. We are currently working with Event Emporium on the next MFAA event so stay tuned for an update.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          7 May 2014
         </time>

           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/crouching-tiger-hidden-dangers/">
             Saving the Sumatran Tiger through music and design
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           Independent music favourites, Portugal the Man, has been enlisted by Smithsonians National Zoo &amp; Conservation Biology Institute to create a song to raise awareness for the plight of the Sumatran Tiger, of which there are only 400 left in the wild.We have worked with our clients at Taronga Zoo on projects both old and new to similarly raise awareness for this beautiful animal.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/crouching-tiger-hidden-dangers/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>

          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="425" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="425" data-imgheight-2="850" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-01-540x425.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-01-1080x850.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">

           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="405" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="405" data-imgheight-2="810" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-03-540x405.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-03-1080x810.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Sumatran tiger at Taronga Zoo" height="637" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-03-850x637.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="307" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="307" data-imgheight-2="614" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-04-540x307.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-04-1080x614.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Event collateral print design collection for Zoofari 210 at Taronga Zoo" height="483" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-04-850x483.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="318" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="318" data-imgheight-2="636" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-05-540x318.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-05-1080x636.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt=" Gala event invitation design featuring tiger illustration" height="501" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/109-091-Tiger-Song-Blog-Post-05-850x501.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Crouching Tiger, Hidden Dangers
          </h2>
          <p>
           Independent music favourites, Portugal the Man, has been enlisted by Smithsonians National Zoo &amp; Conservation Biology Institute to create a song to raise awareness for the plight of the Sumatran Tiger, of which there are only 400 left in the wild. A unique and creative approach to the campaign was needed to bring these tigers back from the brink of extinction.
          </p>
          <p>
           With this vital statistic in mind, only 400 copies of the record were pressed and distributed to famous and otherwise influential people on Earth Day this year. As they listen to the vinyl it degrades over time and the track can only survive if it is digitised. This concept was intrinsically linked to the plight of its subject.
          </p>
          <p>
           We have worked with our clients at Taronga Zoo on projects both old and new to similarly raise awareness for this beautiful animal. In 2010, our
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/projects/year-of-the-tiger/" target="_blank" title="Year of the Tiger">
            Zoofari invitation
           </a>
           used 400 tiny illustrated tigers to demonstrate the fragility of their lives as you held every wild Sumatran Tiger in your hands. For
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/projects/five-for-the-wild/" target="_blank" title="Five for the Wild">
            Zoofari 2012
           </a>
           , our illustrated event collateral continued to raise awareness and funds.
          </p>
          <p>
           This year we have designed a Save the Date postcard for Zoofari 2014, to be followed with an event invitation and collateral for the charity dinner to be held at the Zoo. It will raise funds and awareness for the Tigers, continuing Tarongas commitment to this majestic animal.
          </p>
          <p>
           Recently we were privileged to be taken on a behind-the-scenes tour where we met the Sumatran Tigers of Taronga Zoo. Once you have seen them up close, coupled with some insider knowledge from their keepers, you have a greater empathy for their plight.
          </p>
          <p>
           For more information about the Endangered song project
           <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=btPJDPO-LU4" target="_blank">
            click here
           </a>
           .
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          2 May 2014
         </time>

          </h1>

          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/04/109-076-Sas-Baby-Shower-Blog4-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/04/109-076-Sas-Baby-Shower-Blog4-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="custom branded baby clothing by Another Colour" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/04/109-076-Sas-Baby-Shower-Blog4-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Ready to pop!
          </h2>
          <p>
           Call us suckers for soppy news but we were all smiles when we learnt that client and good friend, Sas Lyon, was pregnant with her first child. When she chose us to help design the invitations to her baby shower we were equally as excited and a little honoured.
          </p>
          <p>
           To know Sas is to know and understand her wicked sense of humour. With this consideration we designed an invitation in the form of a balloon with the cheeky opening line Sas is ready to pop emblazoned across it. The lolly pink balloon (its a girl) had to be blown up by guests in order to read the event details.
          </p>
          <p>
           For the baby-to-be we thought it would be fun to design a custom-made outfit. We used one of our original designs and had this printed on a cotton onesie from American Apparel. Yes, we branded Sass baby but we guess thats okay because she has requested an exact replica in her own size so they can be matching while they watch Peppa Pig together.
          </p>
          <p>
           We are very happy for both Sas and her husband Matt and wish them both the best in the exciting times ahead. Cant wait to meet the little one when she is born! Shes going to be the most stylish (and colourful) baby girl on the block.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Update
          </h2>
          <p>
           Darling Helodie Lyon was born Saturday 12 April 2014. Mother, father and daughter are all well.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          22 April 2014
         </time>

           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/what-colour-should-you-wear-if-you-want-to-win-an-oscar/">
             What colour should you wear if you want to win an Oscar?
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           Its probably safe to say that for most of us the only reason we tune in to the Oscars is for the red carpet spectacle. It's an endless procession of actresses, draped in either the finest couture or fashions most infamous failures. Part runway, part performance and ever-so-slightly ridiculous, it is a guilty indulgence that is best enjoyed with pizza and friends and we never miss it.After many years of avid viewing we decided to turn this obsession into a quantifiable (or informative) pictogram, hoping to learn the science behind these famous frocks.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/what-colour-should-you-wear-if-you-want-to-win-an-oscar/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">
           7 March 2014
          </time>
