          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="388" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="388" data-imgheight-2="777" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V45-540x388.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V45-1080x777.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Oscar winner colours from 1994-2003" height="611" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V45-850x611.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="300" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="300" data-imgheight-2="600" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V47-540x300.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V47-1080x600.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="War of roses" height="472" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V47-850x472.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="388" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="388" data-imgheight-2="777" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V46-540x388.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V46-1080x777.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Oscar winner colours from 2004-2013" height="611" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V46-850x611.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="300" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="300" data-imgheight-2="600" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V411-540x300.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V411-1080x600.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="The good the bd and the ugly" height="472" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/109-037-Oscars-Blog-Experiment-V411-850x472.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <p>
           Its probably safe to say that for most of us the only reason we tune in to the Oscars is for the red carpet spectacle. Its an endless procession of actresses, draped in either the finest couture or fashions most infamous failures. Part runway, part performance and ever-so-slightly ridiculous, it is a guilty indulgence that is best enjoyed with pizza and friends and we never miss it.
          </p>
          <p>
           After many years of avid viewing we decided to turn this obsession into a quantifiable (or informative) pictogram, hoping to learn the science behind these famous frocks. Looking back at the past fifty years (basically from when colour photography was made readily available) we collected images of the winners for Best Actress and Best Supporting Actress to see if there was a winning formula or trend in what the recipients of these awards wore.
          </p>
          <p>
           Each award winners outfit was represented as a single predominant colour. This gave us the first insight into what constitutes a winning dress  the use of single note tones. This might be because, like the Queen of England, it makes it easier to spot them in a crowd. Very rarely did a winner wear more than one colour (different shades of the same colour dont count). In fact, the most colourful dresses to grace the awards stage were not worn by the winners but by someone accepting the award on their behalf  Angela Lansbury in 1984 for Best Supporting winner, Peggy Ashcroft and Raquel Welch in 1969 on behalf of Goldie Hawn. Notable runners up are Halle Berry with her wine-mint-and-flesh Elie Saab gown in 2002 and the rosette-printed floral dress worn by Jessica Tandy in 1989.
          </p>
          <p>
           On a side note, we also began to stocktake the tuxedos that the winning men wore but it wasnt long before we realised that it was all just a thousand shades of black. Aside from Daniel Day-Lewis in 2012 and Christopher Plummer in 2012 who both wore shades of navy blue, it seems that men are incredibly unwilling to break from tradition. Either that or they need more adventurous stylists.
          </p>
          <p>
           The trend we noticed was that black is hands down the reigning colour for the winners, as can be seen in our Pantone-style Oscar swatch set. This may not be all that surprising but it does highlight that a lot of actresses stick to classics and play it safe. Unless youre Cher. Then youll go dressed like youre the Evil Queen from a futuristic fantasy film or the reincarnation of Nefertiti.
          </p>
          <p>
           After classic black came what commentators tend to call old Hollywood glamour or what the rest of us would call metallics  silver and gold tones. This palette includes the dress that Charlize Theron wore when she won her award for playing serial killer Eileen Wernoz in
           <em>
            Monster
           </em>
           and Sandra Bullocks dress from 2009, worn to collect an award for
           <em>
            The Blind Side
           </em>
           .
          </p>
          <p>
           Surprisingly, the grunge-fueled 90s seemed to be when winners were at their most colourful (we were totally expecting the 80s to win this too): Barbie-pink (Gwyneth Paltrow); robin-egg blue (Helen Hunt); mint green (Kim Basinger); and even a lovely rusty velvet (Juliette Binoche).
          </p>
          <p>
           So far, the least colourful times have been well, now. The past decade has seen the winners for both Best Actress and Best Supporting Actress blending into each other with many sticking to safe shades of beige, black and greys with maybe a dash of red or blue. The winners for the past three years have all worn the same neutral colour, albeit in different shades. This probably has something to do with both the the role of the stylist and, more likely, the increasing power of celebrity as a brand.
          </p>
          <p>
           Personally we miss the days when celebrities would turn up looking like a hot mess. Celine Dion wearing a suit backwards; Bjrk in her swan dress and Cher in anything. These dresses stole the limelight for all the wrong reasons, which in our minds, were all the right reasons  because they were fun!
          </p>
          <p>
           <em>
            Images
           </em>
           <a href="http://www.shutterstock.com/" target="_blank">
            Shutterstock
           </a>
           and Wikipedia
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          7 March 2014
         </time>

         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Numskulls Surry Hills street art
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="359" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="359" data-imgheight-2="718" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-015-Blog-Entry-Street-Art1-540x359.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-015-Blog-Entry-Street-Art1-1080x718.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Numskull artwork near Another Colour studio" height="565" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-015-Blog-Entry-Street-Art1-850x565.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="405" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="405" data-imgheight-2="810" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-015-Blog-Entry-Street-Art2-540x405.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-015-Blog-Entry-Street-Art2-1080x810.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Artwork by graffiti artist Numskull" height="637" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-015-Blog-Entry-Street-Art2-850x637.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="381" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="381" data-imgheight-2="763" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-015-Blog-Entry-Street-Art3-540x381.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-015-Blog-Entry-Street-Art3-1080x763.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Artwork by graffiti artist Numskull" height="600" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-015-Blog-Entry-Street-Art3-850x600.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           The word on the street
          </h2>
          <p>
           Right around the corner from our studio is a freshly painted mural from the street artist who goes by the pseudonym of Numskull. In fact, in many of the surrounding streets and on any available surface lives a piece of art whose brush strokes or sprayed droplets are a testament to talented artists working outside of conventional galleries.
          </p>
          <p>
           As a street artist and typographer extraordinaire Numskull brings his art straight to the people. Theres a pearl of wisdom to be found in his popular turns of phrase, illustrated in large scale decoratively painted font displays the world over, on a wall near you.
          </p>
          <p>
           Not only does Numskull do site-specific work like his memorable Taupo, New Zealand mural, which takes its cues from Ghostbusters with the quote when theres something strange in your neighbourhood, he also works from a studio. When he strays from his staple street style he can be seen adorning canvas and paper with cartoonish characters reminiscent of daffy duck or pluto pup, with bulbous eyes peeking out at its viewers.
          </p>
          <p>
           But the one we adore is the one we walk past each day coming to work. What a wonder full day to go painting! he exclaims in giant metre-high letters, and we concur it was. For what he produced on that day conveys his message in succinct, bold type while appearing effortless and fun.
          </p>
          <p>
           For more work by Numskull visit
           <a href="http://www.funskull.com" target="_blank">
            funskull.com
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          6 March 2014
         </time>

          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/happy-birthday-gerald/">
             A minimalist invitation
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           We miss the days when birthday invitations came in the mail. As a formality, they just seemed a little more sincere than your average Facebook tick-list where you discover that youre one amongst four hundred other people that were invited. So when we were contacted to design a custom birthday invite for Gerald Lundgren (the very same Gerald who contacted us to design packaging for the delicious cakes from
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/projects/the-lunetta-baking-company/">
            TheLunetta Baking Company
           </a>
           ) we were excited to see someone else felt the same.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/happy-birthday-gerald/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">
           5 March 2014
          </time>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-happy-birthday-gerald post-hidden-onload post-876" data-postid="876" data-title="A minimalist invitation :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           A minimalist invitation
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-059-Blog-Entry-Gerald-Bday-Card1-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-059-Blog-Entry-Gerald-Bday-Card1-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Invitation design in italian" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-059-Blog-Entry-Gerald-Bday-Card1-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-059-Blog-Entry-Gerald-Bday-Card2-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-059-Blog-Entry-Gerald-Bday-Card2-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="iconography and invitation design" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-059-Blog-Entry-Gerald-Bday-Card2-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-059-Blog-Entry-Gerald-Bday-Card3-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-059-Blog-Entry-Gerald-Bday-Card3-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="italian inspired printed invitation featuring icons" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/109-059-Blog-Entry-Gerald-Bday-Card3-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Happy Birthday Gerald!
          </h2>
          <p>
           We miss the days when birthday invitations came in the mail. As a formality, they just seemed a little more sincere than your average Facebook tick-list where you discover that youre one amongst four hundred other people that were invited. So when we were contacted to design a custom birthday invite for Gerald Lundgren (the very same Gerald who contacted us to design packaging for the delicious cakes from
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/projects/the-lunetta-baking-company/">
            Lunetta Baking Company
           </a>
           ) we were excited to see someone else felt the same.
          </p>
          <p>
           We took a fun, yet minimalist, approach to designing the invite using light pastels for the background and solid black for the type and images. Taking inspiration from Geralds family heritage, the copy for the invite was written completely in Italian (for which we thank Gerald for so kindly translating this and making sure it was all correct). The completed job was then printed up by the ever wonderful guys at Digital Press.
          </p>
          <p>
           We hope you had a great birthday Gerald!
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          5 March 2014
         </time>

           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Cherish our Chimps
          </h2>
          <p>
           Taronga Zoos annual Zoofari gala dinner is something that we are always very proud to be a part of. Their tireless work in conservation and raising awareness about endangered species from across the planet is genuinely inspiring.
          </p>
          <p>
           For 2013, the focus was on the Chimpanzee. Once found in forests throughout Equatorial Africa, the number of chimps in the wild has declined rapidly due to the destruction of habitat and the illegal trade as pets and bushmeat.
          </p>
          <p>
           To create a motif for the event we sourced images from vintage biology books showing Chimpanzees amongst their native flora and, using a collage technique, placed them against backgrounds of muted neutral tones that captured the fragility of not only the Chimpanzee but the forests they need to thrive.
          </p>
          <p>
           E-invites were sent to guests so as to be more environmentally friendly and uncoated, recycled stock was used for the evenings program and collectable postcards. The images from the collateral were then repurposed for the dcor and signage found throughout the event.
          </p>
          <p>
           The event was a huge success, raising a grand total of $297,000 through ticket sales, auctions, raffles and pledges, and will go towards the protection and conservation of the African Chimpanzee.
          </p>
          <p>
           Images courtesy of the Taronga Foundation.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          17 February 2014
         </time>

           The Another Colour Christmas Party  Part 2
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="702" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="702" data-imgheight-2="1404" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/109-049-Aura-Blog-Experiment012-540x702.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/109-049-Aura-Blog-Experiment012-1080x1404.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">

            <img alt="Clint Sawyer for Another Colour in his aura image" height="1105" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/109-049-Aura-Blog-Experiment03-850x1105.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>

           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="702" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="702" data-imgheight-2="1404" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/109-049-Aura-Blog-Experiment05-540x702.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/109-049-Aura-Blog-Experiment05-1080x1404.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Min Writer's aura photograph for another Colour" height="1105" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/109-049-Aura-Blog-Experiment05-850x1105.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Shake it like an aura-filled picture
          </h2>
          <p>
           After testing our fear of heights earlier in the morning (and eating an entire sushi tray apparently intended for twenty people but demolished in no time between the five of us) we were treated to the second part of our day  having our auras photographed.
          </p>
          <p>
           Kirlian photography was first discovered in 1939 by Semyon and Valentina Kirlian who observed that when electrodes were brought near the skin, it caused a faint glow to be perceived. The procedure is said to show a coronal discharge  energy  from objects and people that it captures on film. The colours of the depicted can then be interpreted to show emotional and mental states of the person in the picture.
          </p>
          <p>
           We booked a session with local Kirlian photographer and aura reader, Jann Morgan. The whole setup was admittedly rather fascinating  the camera looked like it belonged to the 18th Century and was attached to two metal plates where you rested your hands and what looked like an old fashioned fax machine. This was used to create an algorithmic measure of the colours found within the aura. This was all set up in front of a wooden stool with a cute, velveteen curtain as background, decorated with some tinsel. It was all rather quaint but still a little daunting what if our aura revealed some deep dark secret?
          </p>
          <p>
           When the process was all done, we put all our photographs in a line to see what our auras apparently look like and the results were rather amusing.
          </p>
          <p>
           With all of us, there was a definite trend towards the warmer end of the spectrum  red, orange, gold and yellow with dashes of pink and green for good measure. Jann explained that these were the more creative colours and that the consistency throughout the group was indicative of why we all get along so well.
          </p>
          <p>
           Then, as we started to compare each individual image, we noticed that some of us were definitely more alike than others. Which is also true in real life.
          </p>
          <p>
           Both Steve and Lauren had solid, bright red auras. This, according to Jann, was the colour of willpower and leadership and the auras of resourceful and creative individuals and while we dont want to say that either of them are stubborn it might just be a little bit true.
          </p>
          <p>
           Next up was Ben, Clint and Min. All three had a lot of orange but, when we looked at them a little closer, each had their own quirks and peculiarities. Which, again, if you have ever met Ben, Clint or Min, this makes complete sense.
          </p>
          <p>
           Bens aura was made up of bright orange, gold and a touch of bright yellow green in the middle  all the colours of creativity, a rather odd sense of humour and a bit of a nerd. Mins aura was orange, pink and red  meaning that she is charismatic, outgoing but abounding in maternalism (which she absolutely is!). Finally, Clints aura was probably the most fun  dubbed the unicorns aura Clint had more colours than the rest of the team put together with orange, red, green, blue and a bit of turquoise for good measure. Creative and outgoing, yet empathic and a bit of a dreamer, this was also the most accurate description of our team.
          </p>
          <p>
           Are we convinced that we are surrounded by a luminous cloud of energy that captures our inner essence? Maybe not. But it was a fun experiment that showed us just one more way that colour can be used to create meaning and express parts of ourselves.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          7 February 2014
         </time>

       <div class="box article-wrapper thumb-slug-trainspotting thumb-823 filter-news filter-project filter-all" data-postid="823">
        <div class="outer-listing">
         <div class="listing">
          <a class="blog-thumb" href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/trainspotting/">
           <figure class="auto-size fade-image bg-color" data-autoheight="166" data-autowidth="250" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="166" data-imgheight-2="333" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo4-250x166.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo4-500x333.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="250" data-imgwidth-2="500">
            <noscript>
             <img alt="" height="166" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo4-250x166.jpg" width="250"/>
            </noscript>
           </figure>
          </a>
          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/trainspotting/">
             Designing for the AusRail Exhibition
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           We recently worked on exhibition materials for Mason Grogan Industrial, which really opened up our eyes to the level of detail that goes into something that we often take for granted  trains, and the materials involved in their production, ensuring we get from A to B in safety and comfort.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/trainspotting/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>

         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Designing for the AusRail Exhibition
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="518" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="518" data-imgheight-2="1036" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo1-540x518.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo1-1080x1036.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">

            <img alt="Brochure design for Mason Grogan Industrial exhibition" height="816" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo1-850x816.jpg" width="850"/>

          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo2-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo2-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">

          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo3-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo3-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Brochure detail for Mason Grogan Industrial" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo3-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>

          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo5-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo5-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Corporate collateral design for Mason Grogan" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo5-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo6-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo6-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Mason Grogan corporate product series design and collateral" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-056-Blog-Entry-MGI-Rail-Expo6-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2 dir="ltr">
           Trainspotting
          </h2>
          <p dir="ltr">
           We recently worked on exhibition materials for Mason Grogan Industrial, which really opened up our eyes to the level of detail that goes into something that we often take for granted  trains, and the materials involved in their production, ensuring we get from A to B in safety and comfort.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Leading up to the AusRAIL industry expo, Mason and Grogan asked us to prepare a set of collateral to showcase the unique, hard-wearing materials of the Industrial rail-focussed branch of their business. Following on from the success of
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/design-feat/" target="_blank">
            the podiatry folder and compendium
           </a>
           , we had big (design) shoes to fill.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           We were tasked with the project of taking a few existing flyers and giving them a refreshed look, and overall consistency, with a modern feel. All nine of which were to be encased in an eye catching folder with a wrap around cover and a spot UV to highlight text and a logo.
          </p>
          <p>
           The interactive space was a lifesize replica of a train carriage, where attendees were able to get on, touch and see the materials in action. The whole experience reminded us a little of going to Questacon in Canberra as kids where you could touch all of the fun things and learn at the same time! Graphics were created for the open plan exhibition panels and a video highlighting key features was produced to complete the experience.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          16 January 2014
         </time>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-dom-perignon-x-jeff-koons post-hidden-onload post-818" data-postid="818" data-title="Dom Prignon X Jeff Koons invitations :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Dom Prignon X Jeff Koons invitations
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="765" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="765" data-imgheight-2="1530" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-060-Blog-Entry-MH-Jeff-Koons1-540x765.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-060-Blog-Entry-MH-Jeff-Koons1-1080x1530.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Promotional card featuring Jeff Koons balloon artwork" height="1204" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-060-Blog-Entry-MH-Jeff-Koons1-850x1204.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-060-Blog-Entry-MH-Jeff-Koons2-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-060-Blog-Entry-MH-Jeff-Koons2-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Promotional design for Dom Prignon featuring Jeff Koons" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-060-Blog-Entry-MH-Jeff-Koons2-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="355" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="355" data-imgheight-2="711" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-060-Blog-Entry-MH-Jeff-Koons31-540x355.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-060-Blog-Entry-MH-Jeff-Koons31-1080x711.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Promotional card featuring pink foiling Dom Prignon" height="559" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-060-Blog-Entry-MH-Jeff-Koons31-850x559.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <p dir="ltr">
           Its not often that you get to work with two of the most renowned names operating within their respective fields but recently we were able to do just that.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Known for their use of high profile artists (previously, they have worked with the likes of Marc Newson and David Lynch), French champagne house Dom Prignon have recently teamed up with American Neo Pop artist, Jeff Koons, to create a limited edition sculpture to showcase their
           <em>
            2003 Vintage Ros
           </em>
           . The result is a metallic hot-pink replication of Koons infamous
           <em>
            Balloon Venus
           </em>
           , a 1.27m high sculpture inspired by the prehistoric
           <em>
            Venus of Willendorf
           </em>
           statue that is considered by many to be an early icon for a fertility goddess and one of the oldest symbols of feminine beauty in Europe. The re-envisioned artwork literally embodies the bottle, opening up to reveal the delicious ros nestled inside. Almost like a delicious pink Transformer!
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Our job in helping launch the collaboration was to create a limited edition postcard that was distributed to VIP clients and patrons. On one side, the postcard depicted the
           <em>
            Balloon Venus
           </em>
           (which sells for a sweet US$20,000 should you be interested in investing) and on the other, the artist himself interacting with the work. To capture the impact of the sculpture, we used a matte black laminate for the background and the image of the sculpture was then embellished with a shiny spot varnish. In keeping with the ros theme, hot pink foiling was used for the text heading and Dom Prignon logo.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           We loved taking part in the project  and not only because we are all avid fans of the odd bottle of Dom and secretly wish to own a Koons or two but because it is not often you get to participate in a project with luminaries of taste and design.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          16 January 2014
         </time>

          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="358" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="358" data-imgheight-2="717" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-050-Trapeze-Blog_5-540x358.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-050-Trapeze-Blog_5-1080x717.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Laurn Finks trapezing" height="564" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-050-Trapeze-Blog_5-850x564.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="358" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="358" data-imgheight-2="717" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-050-Trapeze-Blog_6-540x358.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-050-Trapeze-Blog_6-1080x717.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Steve Scott trapezing" height="564" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-050-Trapeze-Blog_6-850x564.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="358" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="358" data-imgheight-2="717" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-050-Trapeze-Blog_7-540x358.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-050-Trapeze-Blog_7-1080x717.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Another Colour goes trapezing or Christmas 2013" height="564" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/109-050-Trapeze-Blog_7-850x564.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image load-post-image bg-color video" data-autoheight="281" data-autowidth="500" data-bg-color="" data-embed="&lt;iframe src='//player.vimeo.com/video/83646730?color=&amp;portrait=0&amp;byline=0&amp;title=0' width='500' height='281' frameborder='0' webkitallowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen allowfullscreen&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;">
           <div class="overlay bg-color" data-bg-color="">
           </div>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <p dir="ltr">
           According to
           <a href="http://www.buzzfeed.com/video/hillarylevine/surprising-facts-about-creativity" target="_blank">
            Buzzfeed
           </a>
           , creative personalities like to take risks and enjoy getting out of their comfort zones. Then again, according to
           <a href="http://12most.com/2012/03/13/12-striking-tendencies-creative-people/" target="_blank">
            this list
           </a>
           creative people also have all the hallmark signs of having ADD but for now lets just focus on how, for our staff Christmas party, we put the comfort zone theory to the test and passed with flying colours.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           To celebrate a big year full of changes and lots of hard work, the team at Another Colour were treated to a surprise day at
           <a href="https://secure.sydneytrapezeschool.com" target="_blank">
            Sydney Trapeze School
           </a>
           in Tempe. How Steve managed to maintain this secret is beyond us but it was a great trick because in the lead up to the event our imaginations truly got the better of us as we tried to figure out what we were actually going to be doing (paintball, obstacle courses, endurance training and ultimate cage fighting were some of the more interesting ideas that were thrown around). Nicely played Steve, nicely played.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           When all was revealed, to say we were excited would have been a bit of an understatement although, by the looks on some faces, ultimate cage fighting might have been a less confronting option. After a quick introduction with the amazing instructors and a warm up session we were strapped in and ready to go!
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Now, in theory eight metres doesnt sound that high. But when youre forced to climb a rickety metal ladder that wobbles the entire time to reach a platform from which you are meant to jump, it doesnt matter how brave you are or how many ropes are secured to your harness, you get a little scared. And even though some of us had done it before, by the time we reached the top rung of that ladder our hands were damper than a dish rag and our knees were knocking. Maybe it was because, like Buzzfeed suggests, creative types enjoy risk taking or maybe it was because a group of eight-year-old girls were doing it at the same time and our pride got the better of us but no one chickened out.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           After a few practice runs, mastering the legs-up and learning the commands, it was time for the grand finale  the catch. Steve was like a proud stage mum, when we all succeeded in mastering the art of trapeze. Not a single catch was missed thanks to the fantastic direction and encouragement from the STS staff members, although we are convinced that it was our innate athleticism and natural ability that really got us through
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           After a quick stretch and a chuckle as we watched the photos of our day, it was on to the second part of our Christmas Party Challenge. Watch this space to read more about that later
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           We were able to get some videos! Be amazed at our grace. Marvel at our elegant bearing. Laugh at our landings.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          8 January 2014
         </time>

         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Another Colour X Society6
          </h2>
          <p>
           You can now buy Another Colour experiments as a framed print, a tshirt, a laptop skin, a hoodie, a birthday card, an iPhone cover, a baby onesie, a tank top, a throw cushion, a tote bag, a stretched canvas or even a mug!
          </p>
          <p>
           Prints from $15. Tshirts from $20. iPad skins from $20. Totes from $20. Mugs from $15. (Prices in $US)
          </p>
          <p>
           Society6 use American Apparel FineTshirts made with 100% fine jersey cotton combed for softness and comfort. Art prints are on gallery quality natural white, matte, ultra smooth, 100% cotton rag, acid free archival paper.
          </p>
          <p>
           To see the very collectable
           <em>
            Of Curious Creatures
           </em>
           and
           <em>
            When Rodin Met Rozendaal
           </em>
           ranges, visit
           <a href="http://society6.com/AnotherColour" target="_blank">
            society6.com/AnotherColour
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          6 January 2014
         </time>

          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/sweet-ceremony/">
             Sweet Ceremony wedding celebrant branding
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           One of our newest clients, Brigitte Mancini, contacted us all the way from Port Douglas. After receiving her accreditation as a civil servant, Brigitte wanted our help to create an identity and marketing collateral for her company, Sweet Ceremony.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/sweet-ceremony/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">
           12 December 2013
          </time>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-sweet-ceremony post-hidden-onload post-721" data-postid="721" data-title="Sweet Ceremony wedding celebrant branding :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Sweet Ceremony wedding celebrant branding
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="199" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="199" data-imgheight-2="398" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_1-540x199.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_1-1080x398.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Logo design for Brigitte Mancini" height="313" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_1-850x313.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="432" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="432" data-imgheight-2="864" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_2-540x432.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_2-1080x864.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Business card and identity design for Brigitte Mancini" height="680" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_2-850x680.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="432" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="432" data-imgheight-2="864" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_3-540x432.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_3-1080x864.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Brigitte Mancini" height="680" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_3-850x680.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="337" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="337" data-imgheight-2="674" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_4-540x337.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_4-1080x674.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Business card design detail featuring gold and black illustration " height="530" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-045-Sweet-Ceremony-Blog_4-850x530.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <p dir="ltr">
           One of our newest clients, Brigitte Mancini, contacted us all the way from Port Douglas. After receiving her accreditation as a civil servant, Brigitte wanted our help to create an identity and marketing collateral for her company, Sweet Ceremony.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           After talking to Brigitte about her ideas for the business and the direction she wanted it to take, we thought it was important to create an identity that would be suitable for all the services that she provided: not just weddings but funerals, naming ceremonies and vow renewals too. In order to achieve this we decided early on that this meant avoiding the traditional or cliched images or the colour pink. Instead, we chose a bold, black background with a gold filigree pattern to create a contemporary yet classic identity that would be appropriate for all occasions.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Once the job was completed, we thought it would be interesting to have a chat with Brigitte about her experience in starting up a small business and learn what advice she had to offer others who were going through, or about to start, the same process.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           <em>
            Hi Brigitte, thanks for taking the time to chat with us! Can you tell us a little about yourself and Sweet Ceremony?
           </em>
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Well I am 55 years old, wife to a man I have passionately loved for 39 years and a mother to two children who have truly taught me to be a more tolerant and better person, inspiring me to always achieve what I thought was not within my capabilities. I have worked in hospitality for many years and have always thought how wonderful it would be to get into the celebrancy business. I am a hopeless romantic and a strong believer that love can heal almost everything. It was after a conversation with my daughter that it clicked, and in that moment my Sweet Ceremony journey began. The next day I was busy researching courses, starting my own small business and gathering thoughts on what this new business would be called.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           <em>
            What made you want to start your own business?
           </em>
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Since we first got married, I have always operated my husbands air conditioning business. My time in this role was incredibly beneficial because it provided so much knowledge and I learnt so many applicable skills, but you never feel the pride nor the passion you get when youre driving your own affair. When you have your own business you are the recipient of your own criticism and rewards and you are responsible for your improvements and successes. Starting up Sweet Ceremony came when I was ready for a new challenge which allowed me to use all my skills and strengths acquired over my adult life. Sweet Ceremony is also operated from my home office, where I still manage my husbands administrative affairs also. These two roles mean Im lucky to be never doing the same routine all the time  theres never a dull moment and inspiration surrounds me.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           <em>
            When you contacted Another Colour, what were the most important things that you wanted to achieve through dealing with them?
           </em>
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           I approached Steve whilst I was designing my website. I needed and wanted a logo I would be proud of; one that represented my business. The name Sweet Ceremony was reflective of my delivery, and my logo would reflect my style. Its design needed to look how the name sounded but be classy and professional. Another Colour did just that.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Steve supported my thoughts and led me away from some of my initial ideas, and for that I am so grateful for his professional advice. Steve and his team were invaluable with some professional advice and were forthcoming with creative input about the website.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           <em>
            What was the process you followed in creating your company identity? What were the most important elements you wanted represented in the final creation?
           </em>
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           I researched my business online and made a note of each reaction made from each website observed. Some I admired and some I hoped my business would never resemble. The elements I wanted to portray were what my business and services offer, how these are offered and their outcome. Being on the wise and mature side, I am a little reserved with business concepts and ethics. What I wanted to represent was honesty, simplicity, professionalism and style.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           <em>
            How did the team at Another Colour help you achieve this?
           </em>
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           The members of the team I dealt with were approachable, interested and creative. They listened to me and understood exactly what I had in mind but found difficult to describe. Steve knew what I wanted done, and he provided me with new ways of thinking about what I wanted to achieve. Steve and his team got things done quickly and well, and they were extraordinarily helpful at every step. They also came up with a business card that has received endless positive responses. Every recipient of my business card compliments me on its appearance and design and it always manages to get more than just a quick glance and a slide in the pocket. The card is a great conversation starter.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           <em>
            Can you describe your overall experience with Another Colour?
           </em>
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           One of the best decisions I have made on my Sweet Ceremony journey. The identity created by Another Colour is the most crucial business tool I will ever possess that speaks volumes about what I do and who I am. Dealing with Another Colour was about the quality, the promptness, the attention to detail and the effectiveness of their work.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           <em>
            Do you have any advice for other people interested in starting their own business? Or even people who may already have their business and would like to develop their brand more?
           </em>
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           For someone interested in starting up their own business I would advise them to never underestimate their own abilities and potential. You will never know unless you take that step. You are not alone, and sourcing a good creative agency to assist with design and branding will see you succeed.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          12 December 2013
         </time>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-superman-spiderman-and-claude-monet post-hidden-onload post-701" data-postid="701" data-title="Superman, Spiderman and Claude Monet? :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Superman, Spiderman and Claude Monet?
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="489" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="489" data-imgheight-2="979" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_1-540x489.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_1-1080x979.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Superman, Spiderman and Claude Monet?" height="770" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_1-850x770.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="738" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="738" data-imgheight-2="1477" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_21-540x738.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_21-1080x1477.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Superman, Spiderman and Claude Monet?" height="1163" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_21-850x1163.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="481" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="481" data-imgheight-2="962" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_31-540x481.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_31-1080x962.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Superman, Spiderman and Claude Monet?" height="757" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_31-850x757.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="678" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="678" data-imgheight-2="1356" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_41-540x678.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_41-1080x1356.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Superman, Spiderman and Claude Monet?" height="1067" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_41-850x1067.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="674" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="674" data-imgheight-2="1348" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_51-540x674.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_51-1080x1348.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Superman, Spiderman and Claude Monet?" height="1061" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_51-850x1061.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="472" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="472" data-imgheight-2="945" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_61-540x472.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_61-1080x945.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Superman, Spiderman and Claude Monet?" height="744" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/12/109-047-Monet-Blog_61-850x744.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <p>
           He may not have been able to fly like Superman or crawl up walls like Spiderman but apparently Claude Monet did have one thing in common with our two favourite superheroes  super vision.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/the-fiction-faction/" target="_blank">
            We recently posted a story
           </a>
           about the way the human eye perceives colour and in particular the ability for some lucky people to detect more colours than the rest of us (98 million more, to be exact). The idea that some of us are capable of extraordinary forms of perception intrigued us so we started to investigate other vision-related phenomena and found some interesting stories about certain artists. Namely the father of Impressionism, Claude Monet.
          </p>
          <p>
           Famous for his loose, impressionistic style of painting, Monet created controversy in the 19th Century Paris art world for breaking free from traditional painting styles and conventions with his aggressive brush strokes and visible workings of paint. But it was this style of painting that allowed Monet to explore the way natural light affected our perception of colours in the environment.
          </p>
          <p>
           Monets most famous  or most beloved depending on how you look at it  paintings are those done at his cottage gardens outside Paris. Painted later in his career,
           <em>
            Waterlilies, The Artists Garden,
           </em>
           and
           <em>
            The Garden Path
           </em>
           are unique in that they give the viewer an acute insight into the impact that Monets deteriorating eyesight had on his painting. As progressive documentaries of Monets failing eyesight, the paintings in this series grew increasingly darker, filled with deep blues and reds in comparison to the lighter pastels of his early career. It wasnt until 1923 that Monet succumbed to science and finally underwent the surgery that would repair his eyes and enable him to see normally again.
          </p>
          <p>
           According to some
           <a href="http://www.google.com/url?q=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.skepticalartist.com%2F2013%2F06%2F25%2Fclaude-monet-and-ultraviolet-light-did-the-master-impressionist-painter-have-uv-supervision%2F&amp;sa=D&amp;sntz=1&amp;usg=AFQjCNFB6u2JjuY2bYf0lmyVfj00aPrisw" target="_blank">
            theorists from both the art and scientific worlds
           </a>
           , this was the operation that gave Monet more than just his old eyesight. Based upon a comparison of paintings done before and after the surgery of the same scenery, its been argued that this early form of cataract surgery provided Monet the ability to see ultraviolet hues undetectable to the average eye. In fact, those paintings done after the operation show a distinct difference in the way Monet perceived colours. Blues became more vibrant, richer and almost electric, there was much more violet throughout Monets palette than ever before.
          </p>
          <p>
           But apparently this is not an uncommon occurrence in cataract patients.
          </p>
          <p>
           Ultraviolet light exists all around us and the eye contains a lens that filters these rays out. When this lens becomes opaque due to cataracts, surgeries such as the one that Monet had that removes this, ultimately removes the eyes natural UV filter, thus enabling people to see light that they were previously (and naturally, because its harmful) unable to detect. Monets later paintings were consistent with the side-effects reported by other aphakic patients (removal of the eye lens) who all confirmed perception of colours and light that had previously been invisible to the naked eye.
          </p>
          <p>
           We love these kinds of stories, not only because they highlight the supposed hidden superpowers of the human body, but because it also reminds us that when it comes to colour we have barely scratched the surface of what we are capable of seeing.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          10 December 2013
         </time>

          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/the-fiction-faction/">
             Fictional Colours
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           Hooloovoo,Octarine andSquant.Is there really such a thing as a fictional colour?
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/the-fiction-faction/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">
           29 August 2013
          </time>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-the-fiction-faction post-hidden-onload post-688" data-postid="688" data-title="Fictional Colours :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Fictional Colours
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/bookshelf_90-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/bookshelf_90-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Fictional Colours" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/bookshelf_90-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2 dir="ltr">
           The Fiction Faction
          </h2>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Have you ever noticed that when youre reading, the power of your imagination is so intense that it has the ability to recall and replicate certain sensations as theyre described in the book?
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           For example, read about the taste of an apple and your body begins to trick itself into tasting an apple. But what happens when books describe something that the body has never experienced before? Something like a brand new colour?
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Chances are youve never heard of the fourth primary colour Squant, the dark saturated red Sangoire or even the shade of blue called Hooloovoo. But youd be forgiven for such ignorance as these colours only exist in fictional film or literature and the imaginations of its audience. A more infamous example is probably Terry Pratchetts Octarine from his
           <em>
            Discworld
           </em>
           series. In the books, Octarine is the eighth colour of the spectrum, is the colour of magic, and is described as being a greenish yellow-purple colour in other words, impossible to replicate in the real world. Or is it?
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Making up names and describing colours that dont exist isnt such a wild idea. Colour is, after all, a spectrum of perception and there is an enormous variety of shades and hues that the naked human eye cannot perceive. Humans, along with some other primates, are normally trichromatic meaning they have three cone cells in their eyes that are used to pick up colour (red, blue, green). These three cone cells allow us to detect roughly one million hues although on average woman can see up to 50 shades more than the average male. It also doesnt help that more men than women suffer from some form of colour blindness which probably explains why a lot of men need help choosing the right tie each morning.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Recently, however, colour vision researcher Dr Gabriel Jordan in the UK discovered the existence of what she called a tetrachromat  someone who has four cone cells in their eyes. This one additional cone cell means that the owner, a woman, can see 99 million additional colours not visible to the average person. Some of which could potentially be considered a shade of Octarine or Squant?
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Discoveries in colour perception such as this, and similarly other cognitive and visual peculiarities such as Colour Blindness, Synesthesia or Tetrachromacy teach us that colour is never black and white, and cannot be viewed with standardised measures. Unlike humans many animals including some species of spiders, most marsupials, birds, reptiles, and many species of fish, enviably perceive a much wider range of colours.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           When Douglas Adams, author of the
           <em>
            The Hitchhikers Guide to the Galaxy
           </em>
           series speaks of a super intelligent shade of blue he names Hooloovoo, or Reese from
           <em>
            Malcolm in the Middle
           </em>
           mixes blue and yellow to create Blellow, naturally we laugh. But as the world is rich in biodiversity with species yet to be discovered, is it not too much to ask that the colour spectrum is only limited by ourselves and our understanding?
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Next time you are flicking through a science fiction novel, scanning the net or watching some fantastic film that makes reference to an absurd colour, that sight has not seen nor ear heard, pause for a moment and wonder if this colour is science fact, waiting to be proven.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          29 August 2013
         </time>

          <h1 class="project-title">
           Catalogue design for Mason Grogan Medical
          </h1>
         </header>

          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="356" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="356" data-imgheight-2="712" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-006-Blog-Entry-Mason-and-Grogan4-540x356.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-006-Blog-Entry-Mason-and-Grogan4-1080x712.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Exhibition design, signage and event collateral for Mason Grogan Medical" height="561" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-006-Blog-Entry-Mason-and-Grogan4-850x561.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2 dir="ltr">
           Design Feat
          </h2>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Every now and then a project lands on our desk that will at first challenge us with its scope but surprise us with its results. Mason Grogan Medical gave us a collection of dense information that we turned into an easily navigated, beautiful-to-thumb-through product portfolio.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Mason Grogan Medical provide innovative and high performance materials to medical professionals and pride themselves with Materials Intelligence. Aimed at podiatrists with the need for quick, easy to read information, the big challenge for us was to make sure there was both consistency and readily accessible information, whilst appearing well-designed and visually appealing to encourage sales. Sophisticated divider pages showcased macro photography of the technological materials available.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           At the The Australian Podiatry Conference held at the Sydney Convention Centre we designed an interactive exhibition stand that extended the use of the macro photography. Business cards, advertisements, screensavers, flyers and posters that showcased the new-look were also created.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Our clients at Mason Grogan Medical have received overwhelmingly positive feedback from within the company and from clients. We recently received an email from their Managing Director, Meredyth Grogan, saying that the catalogue has already been snapped up by universities as a learning tool.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          19 August 2013
         </time>

          <h1 class="project-title">
           Yves Klein Blue
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-012-Blog-Entry-Eve-Klein-Blue1-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-012-Blog-Entry-Eve-Klein-Blue1-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>

           </noscript>
          </figure>

           <noscript>
            <img alt="Yves Klein Blue" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-012-Blog-Entry-Eve-Klein-Blue41-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           The Blue Bias
          </h2>
          <p>
           <em>
            For me, each nuance of a color is in some way an individual, a being who is not only from the same race as the base color, but who definitely possesses a distinct character and personal soul.
           </em>
           Yves Klein
          </p>
          <p>
           Its hard to imagine a career based upon the use of a single colour but thats exactly what French artist, Yves Klein, did. In response to what Klein said was a complete misinterpretation to an exhibition that explored a range of monochrome textures, and thus began an era in his art that focused on the exploration of one colour only  blue.
          </p>
          <p>
           This era, known as the Blue Epoch, was to become Kleins legacy to the art world. Not only did it revel in going against the established notions of art and practice, but it was also the setting for the creation of Yves Klein Blue, or as he called it, IKB International Klein Blue. For an exhibition held in Milan, Klein  with the aid of friend and paint dealer Edouard Adam  created a unique ultramarine pigment that resembled the bright blue once created by crushed lapis lazuli in religious iconography.
          </p>
          <p>
           This bright, almost electric, blue was created through suspending the ultramarine pigment in a synthetic resin known as Rhodopas, or what Klein was to call The Medium. This allowed the pigment to retain its natural brilliance that, when used in traditional linseed oils, would often be rendered dull. For the exhibition, Klein applied the paint in a thick, layered technique across eleven canvases that surrounded the viewer in a sea of bright, iridescent blues. To promote the exhibition, Klein released 1001 blue balloons and sent out postcards with stamps of IKB attached that he had bribed the local post office to accept as legitimate. That is colour dedication right there!
          </p>
          <p>
           Klein went about applying this blue to various approaches to art  appropriating mass-produced recreations of famous sculptures, he painted them with his shade of blue and turned them into something rather alien and uncanny. He painted the bodies of women who then rolled themselves across large sheets of canvas and paper laid out on the floor  capturing their curves and motion in an electric, vivid blue process of movement.
          </p>
          <p>
           For us, that something as simple as the colour blue could be used to revolutionise the art world is incredibly inspiring. We particularly appreciate Kleins obsession with the impact of colour and the idea that colour can still be an area for the development of groundbreaking ideas.
          </p>
          <p>
           Sources:
           <br/>
           <a href="http://www.theartstory.org/artist-klein-yves.htm" target="_blank">
            theartstory.org/artist-klein-yves
            <br/>
           </a>
           <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yves_Klein" target="_blank">
            en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yves_Klein
            <br/>
           </a>
           <a href="http://www.yveskleinarchives.org/documents/bio_us.html">
            yveskleinarchives.org
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           Image 1,Yves Klein, 1961. Yves Klein Archives. Photo by Charles Wilp.
           <br/>
           Image 3,
           <em>
            With the Void
           </em>
           , Full Powers at The Hirshhorn Museum and Sculpture Garden
           <br/>
           Image 4,
           <em>
            Venus Bleue
           </em>
           , Yves Klein.
           <br/>
           Image 5,
           <em>
            1001BlueBalloons Release
           </em>
           . Vincen T
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          16 August 2013
         </time>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-cartoon-connection post-hidden-onload post-657" data-postid="657" data-title="Creating a how-to animation for a new product :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
