         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Creating a how-to animation for a new product
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="359" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="359" data-imgheight-2="719" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-022-Blog-Entry-IStageEvent_01-540x359.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-022-Blog-Entry-IStageEvent_01-1080x719.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Iconography series by Another Colours" height="565" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-022-Blog-Entry-IStageEvent_01-850x565.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="325" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="325" data-imgheight-2="651" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-022-Blog-Entry-IStageEvent_02-540x325.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-022-Blog-Entry-IStageEvent_02-1080x651.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Corporate Collateral featuring iconography" height="512" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-022-Blog-Entry-IStageEvent_02-850x512.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image load-post-image bg-color video" data-autoheight="281" data-autowidth="500" data-bg-color="" data-embed="&lt;iframe src='http://player.vimeo.com/video/72013190?color=&amp;portrait=0&amp;byline=0&amp;title=0' width='500' height='281' frameborder='0' webkitAllowFullScreen mozallowfullscreen allowFullScreen&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;">
           <div class="overlay bg-color" data-bg-color="">
           </div>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2 dir="ltr">
           Cartoon Connection
          </h2>
          <p dir="ltr">
           How do you make an event app more fun? Just add colour, and movement.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           To help relaunch their event app, IStageEvent, Staging Connections asked us to develop a suite of e-brochures and a video that explained the apps features and benefits. IStageEvent is designed to replace the traditional (and rather wasteful) paper flyers handed out at events and conferences. It informs you of keynote speakers, schedules, site-maps and bios, all in the one place, and keeps you up to date with reminders and any last minute changes to the program.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           When approaching this brief, we needed something that was entertaining, communicated clearly and stayed in line with the Staging Connections brand. During this workshopping process we remembered how we learnt most things while we were growing up  cartoons!
          </p>
          <p>
           Using Adobe Illustrator and Adobe After Effects, we created a short video that used simple white icons and colourful backdrops. We developed a soundtrack to play in the background and collaborated with the Marketing Team to create an appropriate script with vocal talents provided by one of their tech guys. It was a lot of fun making the illustrations pop, zoom about and come to life on the screen.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          12 August 2013
         </time>

          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/test-patterns/">
             Test Patterns
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           Some of us here at Another Colour are old enough to remember when television stations actually turned off late at night. There would literally be nothing but test patterns across all channels until 5am when the early morning news and cartoons would begin.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/test-patterns/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">
           8 August 2013
          </time>
          <aside>
           <ul>
            <li class="inspiration">
             <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/filter/inspiration/">
             </a>
            </li>
           </ul>
          </aside>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-test-patterns post-hidden-onload post-660" data-postid="660" data-title="Test Patterns :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Test Patterns
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="393" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="393" data-imgheight-2="786" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-003-AC_test-pattern_BLOG-540x393.png" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-003-AC_test-pattern_BLOG-1080x786.png" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Test Patterns" height="619" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/109-003-AC_test-pattern_BLOG-850x619.png" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="720" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="720" data-imgheight-2="1440" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/AC_IMG_5014_rt1-540x720.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/AC_IMG_5014_rt1-1080x1440.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Test Patterns" height="1133" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/AC_IMG_5014_rt1-850x1133.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="720" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="720" data-imgheight-2="1440" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/AC-test-patter-540x720.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/AC-test-patter-1080x1440.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Test Patterns" height="1133" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/AC-test-patter-850x1133.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image load-post-image bg-color video" data-autoheight="281" data-autowidth="500" data-bg-color="" data-embed="&lt;iframe src='http://player.vimeo.com/video/71965659?color=&amp;portrait=0&amp;byline=0&amp;title=0' width='500' height='281' frameborder='0' webkitAllowFullScreen mozallowfullscreen allowFullScreen&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;">
           <div class="overlay bg-color" data-bg-color="">
           </div>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <p dir="ltr">
           Some of us here at Another Colour are old enough to remember when television stations actually turned off late at night. There would literally be nothing but test patterns across all channels until 5am when the early morning news and cartoons would begin. And while they might not have intended to be, the geometric shapes and combinations of colour were a lot of fun. They inspired us to make our own test pattern for the Coming Soon holding page of this website. With our own twist, of course.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Recently, we had the pleasure of experiencing an altogether different kind of test pattern. As part of the ISEA (International Symposium of Electronic Art) and Vivid Live festivals, Japanese artist Ryoji Ikeda turned one of the halls at Redferns Carriageworks into a large, interactive light- and sound-scape that was called
           <em>
            Test Pattern #5
           </em>
           , an immersive audio-visual installation inspired by computer programming data which converts information into barcode and binary patterns.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           To say it was overwhelming would be an understatement. As soon as we walked in, we were immersed in a room that was filled by a thumping bass and overlapped with digital sounds. These sounds were then translated into a corresponding digital light show that ran down the middle of the room where you were invited to stand (or run as some of the kids clearly loved doing). It was disorientating, mind-blowing and completely amazing all at the same time. One of the most interesting parts was watching people move, as their bodies seemed to jump from one spot to another making their way through the juxtaposing lights of the installation.
          </p>
          <p>
           We captured a little of it on video where you can catch a glimpse of our resident writer, Ben, hidden amongst all the other kids. Warning: loud!
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          8 August 2013
         </time>

          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/another-colour-our-new-identity/">
             Another Colour  our new identity
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           Welcome to the very first entry of our new blog on our new website to celebrate our new identity, Another Colour. This will be a place where we will share news, updates on current projects, what inspires us, ideas, and all of our random thoughts and thinks about the wonderful industry we work in.
          </p>
          <p>
           But first things first  why the change?
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/another-colour-our-new-identity/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">
           16 July 2013
          </time>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-another-colour-our-new-identity post-hidden-onload post-387" data-postid="387" data-title="Another Colour  our new identity :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Another Colour  our new identity
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="540" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="540" data-imgheight-2="1000" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-splash-page-540x540.gif" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-splash-page.gif" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1000">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Another Colour  our new identity" height="850" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-splash-page-850x850.gif" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <p>
           Welcome to the very first entry of our new blog on our new website to celebrate our new identity, Another Colour. This will be a place where we will share news, updates on current projects, what inspires us, ideas, and all of our random thoughts and thinks about the wonderful industry we work in.
          </p>
          <p>
           But first things first  why the change? Whilst we still offer the same quality of work and service, we felt that we had reached a point where we had outgrown the simplicity that Steve Scott Graphic Design implied. And for several reasons.
          </p>
          <p>
           The most obvious was that we had become just that  a we. Eight years after its humble beginnings in a home office in Darlinghurst, SSGD had grown to become a collective of creative people. This has also meant that we have definitely outgrown our living room, and we now occupy a sparkling new office in Surry Hills at the Interchange (fun fact  the studios are owned by the one and only Ken Done) and a satellite office in Melbourne.
          </p>
          <p>
           Secondly, as the nature of the industry and the requirements of our clients changed, so have our range of services and skills developed in tangent. More than half of our work is now online: websites, social media and electronic direct marketing.
          </p>
          <p>
           Thirdly, our no frills name wasnt inspiring  we thought it needed to be changed to reflect the scope of what we now do. Add to the fact that it also created the longest ever email address! SSGD had finally reached a point where it was no longer represented who we had become.
          </p>
          <p>
           And we think that Another Colour does exactly that. Its about seeing things in another light. Its about being a different studio  embracing the challenges that come with your project and understanding pragmatism and creativity are not mutually exclusive. Its also about never forgetting to have fun with what we do  to play, experiment and learn whilst doing so.
          </p>
          <p>
           This isnt just a website about our new identity and the work we do. Its a place where we hope to share, discuss and inspire. It will be our gallery, our laboratory and our playground. We hope you visit us often.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          16 July 2013
         </time>

       <div class="box article-wrapper thumb-slug-how-to-name-a-studio thumb-319 filter-inspiration filter-news filter-project filter-all" data-postid="319">
        <div class="outer-listing">
         <div class="listing">
          <a class="blog-thumb" href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/how-to-name-a-studio/">
           <figure class="auto-size fade-image bg-color" data-autoheight="166" data-autowidth="250" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="166" data-imgheight-2="333" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-1-250x166.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-1-500x333.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="250" data-imgwidth-2="500">

             <img alt="" height="166" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-1-250x166.jpg" width="250"/>

           </figure>
          </a>
          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/how-to-name-a-studio/">
             How to name a design studio
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           Over the years we have been involved in many naming projects: from company names to more fleeting names such as those used to brand an event or a campaign. By far the hardest naming project has been re-naming ourselves: from Steve Scott Graphic Design to Another Colour.
          </p>
          <p>
           So how do we go about choosing a name? There are five phases to our naming projects.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/how-to-name-a-studio/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">
           18 June 2013
          </time>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-how-to-name-a-studio post-hidden-onload post-319" data-postid="319" data-title="How to name a design studio :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           How to name a design studio
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-1-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-1-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="How to name a design studio" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-1-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-2-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-2-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="How to name a design studio" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-2-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-3-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-3-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="How to name a design studio" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-3-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="360" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="360" data-imgheight-2="720" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-4-540x360.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-4-1080x720.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="How to name a design studio" height="566" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Studio-Name-4-850x566.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           The fourphases of namingour design studio
          </h2>
          <p>
           Over the years we have been involved in many naming projects: from company names to more fleeting names such as those used to brand an event or a campaign. By far the hardest naming project has been re-naming ourselves: from Steve Scott Graphic Design to Another Colour.
          </p>
          <p>
           So how do we go about choosing a name? There are four phases to our naming projects.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Phase one  the assessment
          </h2>
          <p>
           Sometimes you just feel like a change: you might get a haircut, or buy a colourful pair of sneakers. But you rarely change your name (unless youre on the run). So why did we do it?
          </p>
          <p>
           This was something that we thought about long and hard. Do we really need a new name? Or do we just need a new look? What were the pros and cons? Changing our name could be costly  registering the new name, updating stationery, changing signage and relaunching our website all adds up. Would we lose all our brand equity that we have built up? After months of discussion we decided that a new name should really only be adopted if our current name was truly ineffective. And since it no longer was (read about that story
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/another-colour-our-new-identity/" title="Another Colour  our new identity">
            here
           </a>
           ) we decided to take up the challenge.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Phase two  the word map
          </h2>
          <p>
           To come up with a name, we started a list. Anytime we heard a word we liked we added it to the list. It didnt have to be for any reason in particular  could have been spotted on the side of an ice-cream truck. If we liked it, we just added it. Seeing words from other team members often catalysed a string of new words that were completely unexpected. We used
           <a href="http://www.wordnik.com/" target="_blank" title="Wordnik">
            wordnik
           </a>
           to uncover synonyms and hyponyms. Then we paired different words for poetic effect: rhymes, alliteration, consonance and assonance. We looked for words that had multiple meanings, words that were relevant to our business and words that were euphonic.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Phase three  the shortlist
          </h2>
          <p>
           In reality, this was actually a longlist. A very long list. We toyed with numerous ideas that ranged from the technical (
           <em>
            Flux, Twindragon, Vertex
           </em>
           ), to cute (
           <em>
            Lost Mittens, Ugly Duckling, Plastic Kitten
           </em>
           ), to random (
           <em>
            Blushing Crow
           </em>
           ). Old names (
           <em>
            Loom, Challice, Harbinger, Talisman
           </em>
           ) and names we made up (
           <em>
            Vixo, Ography
           </em>
           ). Pretty names (
           <em>
            Gossamer, Lucent, Inkling, Meld
           </em>
           ) and ugly names (
           <em>
            Concoction, Fat Lattice
           </em>
           ). Word plays (
           <em>
            Hue Diligence, About Space, Colourbind
           </em>
           ) to names that were poetic (
           <em>
            Rubber Hydra, Shapeshift
           </em>
           ). We really liked
           <em>
            Playpen
           </em>
           (we play with pens)  but googling that kept bringing up porn.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Phase four  trying it on
          </h2>
          <p>
           When we finally settled on Another Colour, we put it through
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/the-naming-checklist/" title="The Naming Checklist">
            The Checklist
           </a>
           , a series of questions we ask to ensure the success of a new name. We ran the name past a test group to see it there were any pitfalls.
          </p>
          <p>
           We stuck it up on the pin board in our studio in large letters and over the next few weeks it became a little shrine that we looked at every day as we tried to decide if it suited us. Gradually, the cheeky half-rhyme grew on us more and more and it inspired a lot of other ideas to roll out with our new identity.
          </p>
          <p>
           We liked the many different and relevant meanings the name could convey. It highlighted the ways we do things differently from our competitors  offering both creativity and pragmatism to all our projects. It also represented the importance of having fun with design and a celebration of colour. One of our favourite aspects of the name is that on each page of our website our logo literally becomes, another colour.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          18 June 2013
         </time>

          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/the-naming-checklist/">
             Naming a company? Run it past this checklist
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p dir='"""""ltr"""""'>
           Choosing a new name for your business or product is a big decision and an article we often refer to is Steve Harringtons
           <em>
            How to Nail a Name
           </em>
           (Sydney Morning Herald, 17 November 2011). Steve provides a very concise and helpful checklist to make sure your name is well chosen and fits your criteria. When we are whittling down a long list of names we have brainstormed for a naming project we run them through each of these items to make sure that any pitfalls of the name are established.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/the-naming-checklist/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">
           17 June 2013
          </time>
          <aside>
           <ul>
            <li class="inspiration">
             <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/filter/inspiration/">
             </a>
            </li>
           </ul>
          </aside>
         </div>

       </div>
       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-the-naming-checklist post-hidden-onload post-325" data-postid="325" data-title="Naming a company? Run it past this checklist :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Naming a company? Run it past this checklist
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="342" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="342" data-imgheight-2="684" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/cabbage-patch-540x342.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/cabbage-patch-1080x684.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Naming a company? Run it past this checklist" height="539" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/cabbage-patch-850x539.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2 dir="ltr">
           The naming checklist
          </h2>
          <p dir="ltr">
           Choosing a new name for your business or product is a big decision and an article we often refer to is Steve Harringtons
           <em>
            How to Nail a Name
           </em>
           (Sydney Morning Herald, 17 November 2011). Steve provides a very concise and helpful checklist to make sure your name is well chosen and fits your criteria. When we are whittling down a long list of names we have brainstormed for a naming project we run them through each of these items to make sure that any pitfalls of the name are established.
          </p>
          <p dir="ltr">
           1. Keep it simple.
           <br/>
           2. Keep it short.
           <br/>
           3. Will it stand the test of time?
           <br/>
           4. Does it resonate with the target market?
           <br/>
           5. Can it be easily pronounced?
           <br/>
           6. Can it be twisted around by a mischievous journalist?
           <br/>
           7. Consider cultural sensitivities?
           <br/>
           8. Does it have layers of meaning?
           <br/>
           9. Never chose the first name you like (people are likely to pick the familiar over the new).
           <br/>
           10. Be prepared for people to hate it at first (it can take time).
          </p>
          <p>
           Through our own experience we have added the following:
          </p>
          <p>
           11. Is it unique and original?
           <br/>
           12. Is a url available?
           <br/>
           13. Try the say it back to me test. Say the name to a friend and ask them to repeat it back to you. If they say what? or huh? it might not be the most effective. If youve made up a word, phonetic spelling may help (
           <em>
            Google, Accor
           </em>
           ).
           <br/>
           14. Is it memorable? Alliteration (
           <em>
            American Apparel
           </em>
           ), onomatopoeia (
           <em>
            Bing, Snap
           </em>
           ), consonance (
           <em>
            Kodak, Twitter
           </em>
           ), rhymes (
           <em>
            7Eleven
           </em>
           ), half rhymes (
           <em>
            Another Colour
           </em>
           ) and wordplays (
           <em>
            Avant Card
           </em>
           ) can help.
           <br/>
           15. Think twice about phunky spelling of everyday words (
           <em>
            Kwik Kopy
           </em>
           ). It can help people find you on google, but it can be hard to remember.
           <br/>
           16. Avoid highly generic names that are forgettable and hard to give personality.
           <br/>
           17. Does it allow for future growth?
           <em>
            Burger King
           </em>
           will always be associated with burgers but
           <em>
            McDonalds
           </em>
           have more opportunity to diversify.
           <br/>
           18. Does the name have positive connotations?
           <br/>
           19. Avoid old tricks. Acronyms (
           <em>
            BMW, IBM
           </em>
           ), spaceless names (
           <em>
            FedEx, TeamWorks
           </em>
           ) and Web 2.0 (
           <em>
            flickr, tumblr
           </em>
           ) have been done to death.
           <br/>
           20. Whats your gut reaction? Do you like it? Is it you? Even if you tick 1 to 19, this is the most important.
          </p>
          <p>
           At the beginning of the renaming process, its important not to confine yourself during word mapping sessions so you can allow for full creativity to flow. (
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/how-to-name-a-studio/" title="How To Name A Studio">
            How to name a studio
           </a>
           tells the process we used for Another Colour.) This is a great checklist to use at the end to whittle down your options and find a robust solution.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          17 June 2013
         </time>

           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/its-not-easy-being-green/">
             Chartreuse  the divisive colour
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           <em>
            There isn't a colour I wouldn't use except Chartreuse.
           </em>
           Seymour Chwast, American graphic designer, illustrator, and type designer.
          </p>
          <p>
           Many would agree. Reminiscent of slime, snot, pus or that 80s fluoro top you used to own, there can be very primal objections to the colour chartreuse.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/its-not-easy-being-green/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>

       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-its-not-easy-being-green post-hidden-onload post-309" data-postid="309" data-title="Chartreuse  the divisive colour :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Chartreuse  the divisive colour
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="364" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="364" data-imgheight-2="729" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Chatreuse2-540x364.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Chatreuse2-1080x729.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Chartreuse  the divisive colour" height="573" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-Chatreuse2-850x573.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <h2>
           Its not easy being green
          </h2>
          <p>
           <em>
            There isnt a colour I wouldnt use except Chartreuse.
           </em>
           Seymour Chwast, American graphic designer, illustrator, and type designer.
          </p>
          <p>
           Many would agree. Reminiscent of slime, snot, pus or that 80s fluoro top you used to own, there can be very primal objections to the colour chartreuse.
          </p>
          <p>
           For such a bold, brassy colour it has a name born from humble origins. The
           <a href="http://www.chartreuse.fr/">
            Chartreuse
           </a>
           liqueur website explains that the French word chartreuse means charter house  the monasteries that the monks of the Carthusian order live in, who started producing the liqueur in 1764. Made with 130 secret ingredients, chartreuse was originally sold as an elixir, or medicine.
          </p>
          <p>
           When you taste the liqueur one can pick up subtle hints of honey, native herbs and aromatic floral notes. These notes also translate visually creating a complex construction of shades. Chartreuse is known for its emotive qualities such as flexibility, growth and expansion (Jane Meredith Adams,
           <em>
            Natural Solutions
           </em>
           magazine).
          </p>
          <p>
           If you still hate chartreuse then maybe its not the colour, maybe you are just a plain jane, vanilla loving, neutral-ist. We love chartreuse for its story, its energy and because its a colour that moves you.
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          15 June 2013
         </time>

       <div class="box article-wrapper thumb-slug-music-to-design-by thumb-311 filter-inspiration filter-all" data-postid="311">
        <div class="outer-listing">
         <div class="listing">
          <a class="blog-thumb" href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/music-to-design-by/">
           <figure class="auto-size fade-image bg-color" data-autoheight="250" data-autowidth="250" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="250" data-imgheight-2="500" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-13-5-Blog-Entry-Studio-Music-250x250.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-13-5-Blog-Entry-Studio-Music-500x500.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="250" data-imgwidth-2="500">
            <noscript>
             <img alt="" height="250" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-13-5-Blog-Entry-Studio-Music-250x250.jpg" width="250"/>
            </noscript>
           </figure>
          </a>
          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/music-to-design-by/">
             Music to design by
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           Music is an integral part of our nine to five here at Another Colour. From the moment we step in the door each morning til the lights go out, its winding its way out of the speakers and into the studio. Bringing us anything from the relentless minimal electro beat of Robyns
           <em>
            Dancing On My Own
           </em>
           to the raw unfettered sounds of an acoustic guitar on the latest album by Wavves; a high soprano on Bjrks
           <em>
            Homogenic
           </em>
           or the syncopated rhyming of MIA on a track like
           <em>
            Bamboo Banga
           </em>
           . And then everything in between.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/music-to-design-by/">
            Read more
           </a>
          </p>
          <time class="blog-footer">
           15 June 2013
          </time>
          <aside>
           <ul>
            <li class="inspiration">
             <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/filter/inspiration/">
             </a>
            </li>
           </ul>
          </aside>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div aria-hidden="true" class="outer-full-article post-slug-music-to-design-by post-hidden-onload post-311" data-postid="311" data-title="Music to design by :: Graphic Design Sydney :: Another Colour" role="presentation">
        <article class="full-article">
         <a class="close-button" href="#">
          Close
         </a>
         <header>
          <h1 class="project-title">
           Music to design by
          </h1>
         </header>
         <div class="image-wrapper">
          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="540" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="540" data-imgheight-2="1080" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-13-5-Blog-Entry-Studio-Music-540x540.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-13-5-Blog-Entry-Studio-Music-1080x1080.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Music to design by" height="850" src="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/AC-13-5-Blog-Entry-Studio-Music-850x850.jpg" width="850"/>
           </noscript>
          </figure>
         </div>
         <div class="article-body">
          <p>
           Music is an integral part of our nine to five here at Another Colour. From the moment we step in the door each morning til the lights go out, its winding its way out of the speakers and into the studio. Bringing us anything from the relentless minimal electro beat of Robyns
           <em>
            Dancing On My Own
           </em>
           to the raw unfettered sounds of an acoustic guitar on the latest album by Wavves; a high soprano on Bjrks
           <em>
            Homogenic
           </em>
           or the syncopated rhyming of MIA on a track like
           <em>
            Bamboo Banga
           </em>
           . And then everything in between.
          </p>
          <p>
           Sometimes it can be found in the background but often it creeps to the fore when we least expect it and especially when our favourite song comes on  we could listen LCD Soundsystems
           <em>
            Someone Great
           </em>
           ad nauseum.
          </p>
          <p>
           Its there when we choose that corporate colour palette or refine a new brands identity, its providing the essential back beat to keep us well paced on a tough project or simply making ourselves that first, second or third cup of coffee to get us through the day.
          </p>
          <p>
           Few rules govern our selection of this daily soundtrack, but the need for variety and a thirst for the new oversee all playlists. Old, new, male, female, fast then slow, the hyped (Daft Punks
           <em>
            Random Access Memories
           </em>
           ) and the underplayed (anything by Alpine), sparse for a moment and a wall of sound the next. We never press pause because the music never stops.
          </p>
          <h3>
           Currently Serenading Our Ears
          </h3>
          <p>
           <em>
            Body Talk Part 2
           </em>
           Robyn
           <br/>
           <em>
            Random Access Memories
           </em>
           Daft Punk
           <br/>
           <em>
            Homogenic
           </em>
           Bjrk
           <br/>
           <em>
            Under The Pink
           </em>
           Tori Amos
           <br/>
           <em>
            A is for Alpine
           </em>
           Alpine
           <em>
           </em>
           <br/>
           <em>
            This is Happening
           </em>
           LCD Soundsystem
           <br/>
           <em>
            Sgt. Peppers Lonely Hearts Club Band
           </em>
           The Beatles
           <br/>
           <em>
            Afraid of Heights
           </em>
           Wavves
           <br/>
           <em>
            Kala
           </em>
           MIA
          </p>
         </div>
         <time class="blog-footer">
          15 June 2013
         </time>

          <header>
           <h2 class="blog-title">
            <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/society6-in-the-studio/">
             Society6 in the design studio
            </a>
           </h2>
          </header>
          <p>
           After moving to our new space we needed to deck it out with some colour and personality. We found these prints on
           <a href='"http://society6.com/"' target='"_blank"'>
            Society6
           </a>
           . Yes that is Arnold from Diffrent Strokes! Great artwork by up and coming artists as well as studios. Affordable artwork in the form of prints, canvases, cushions, iPhone covers and tshirts.
           <a href="http://anothercolour.com.au/blog/society6-in-the-studio/">

           </a>

           Society6 in the design studio
          </h1>
         </header>

          <figure class="auto-size fade-post-image bg-color" data-autoheight="230" data-autowidth="540" data-bg-color="#cccccc" data-imgheight-1="230" data-imgheight-2="461" data-imgurl-1="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/109-007-Blog-Entry-Studio-Art_03-540x230.jpg" data-imgurl-2="http://anothercolour.com.au/ac-cms/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/109-007-Blog-Entry-Studio-Art_03-1080x461.jpg" data-imgwidth-1="540" data-imgwidth-2="1080">

         <div class="article-body">
          <p>
           After moving to our new space we needed to deck it out with some colour and personality. We found these prints on
           <a href="http://society6.com/" target="_blank" title="Society6">
            Society6
           </a>
           . Yes that is Arnold from Diffrent Strokes! Great artwork by up and coming artists as well as studios. Affordable artwork in the form of prints, canvases, cushions, iPhone covers and tshirts.
          </p>
          <p>
           Credits from top to bottom:
          </p>

            Another Colour Shop
           </a>
           on Society6.
